When the Shafi' Ratifies the Sale from the Seller's Side: Loss of Pre-Emption Right
Explains that a shafi' loses pre-emption if he ratifies the sale from the seller's side.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the rule for when a shafi' loses the right of pre-emption and apply it to scenarios involving a guarantee or an option to ratify the sale.

Core Idea
If the shafi' himself completes the sale from the seller's side, his pre-emption right is lost.

This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah clarifies a critical limitation on the right of pre-emption (shuf'ah). While the shafi' generally has the right to step into the buyer's shoes, that right is forfeited if the shafi' himself was instrumental in finalizing the sale on behalf of the seller. We will examine two specific contexts: when the shafi' acts as a guarantor for the seller, and when the seller stipulates an option for the shafi' to ratify the sale.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
What is the act being discussed? It is the claim of shuf'ah (pre-emption) by a person who is also the shafi'. The ruling is that he loses that right in certain conditions.
The act is not a sale itself but the exercise of a legal option.
2
Identify the two scenarios that cause loss
The text mentions two scenarios: (1) the shafi' is a guarantor (damin) for the seller's obligation to deliver the property or compensate the buyer; (2) the seller stipulates an option (khiyar) for the shafi' to ratify the sale, and the shafi' does so.
Both scenarios involve the shafi' acting on behalf of the seller.
3
Contrast with the buyer's side
The text notes that if the option is given to the shafi' by the buyer, and the shafi' ratifies the purchase, he retains his pre-emption right. This is because his act is one of buying, not selling.
The key is whose side the shafi' confirms.
4
Trace the reasoning
The reasoning is that by ratifying or guaranteeing the sale from the seller's side, the shafi' has effectively made the sale final. It would be contradictory for him to then claim pre-emption to undo that same sale.
The principle: one cannot both cause a transaction and then claim to revoke it.
5
Apply to hypotheticals
Given a scenario, determine whether the shafi' lost or retains his right based on whose side he acted on.
Practice with the examples in the source.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المشروط له الخيار البيع وهو الشفيع فلا شفعة له لان البيع تم بامضائه بخلاف جانب المشروط له الخيار من جانب المشترى. ترجمہ اور ایسے ہی اگر ضامن ہو گیا کوئی شخص بائع کی جانب سے تاوان و خسارہ کا اور وہی شفیع ہے تو اس کے لئے شفعہ نہیں ہے اور ایسے ہی جبکہ بائع نے بیچا اپنے غیر کیلئے اور خیار کی شرط کی ہو اور مشروطالہ الخیار نے بیع کو نافذ کر دیا اور وہی شفیع ہو تو اس کو شفعہ نہیں ملے گا اسلئے کہ بیع اس کے نافذ کرنے کی وجہ سے نام ہوئی ہے۔ بخلاف مشروطالہ الخیار کی جانب کے مشتری کی جانب سے۔ تشریح مشتری کوئی مکان خریدنا چاہتا ہے مگر اس کو اس میں کچھ تردد ہے کہ شاید اس میں کوئی استحقاق کا دعوی کر دے یا کوئی اور تاوان و خسارہ کی صورت سامنے آجائے ۔ مگر زید نے بائع کی جانب سے ضانت لی اور مشتری سے کہا کہ تو بے فکر ہوکر خرید لے اگر کوئی تاوان والی بات سامنے آئی تو میں اس کا ضامن ہوں کہ یہ مکان تمہارے حوالہ کردوں۔ یا بالفرض مکان دینے سے عاجز ہو جاؤں تو اس کی قیمت تمہارے حوالہ کر دوں اور اتفاق سے یہی زید اس گھر کا شفیع بھی ہے تو اب زید کوشفعہ نہیں ملے گا اس لئے کہ اس کی جانب سے بیج نام ہوئی تھی اور اس کی جانب سے اس کو توڑنا لازم آئے گا۔ ایک شخص نے اپنا مکان فروخت کیا مگر اس نے اپنے دوست زید کیلئے خیار کی شرط لگائی اور زید نے بیع کو نافذ کر دیا اتفاق سے یہی زید گھر کا شفیع بھی ہے تو اب زید کو شفعہ نہیں ملے گا اسی دلیل سابق کی وجہ سے۔ ہاں اگر مشتری نے کوئی مکان خریدا اور اس نے زید کیلئے خیار شرط لگائی اور زید نے شراء کو نافذ کر دیا اور اتفاق سے یہی زید گھر کا شفیع بھی ہے تو اس صورت میں زید کو شفعہ ملے گا کیونکہ یہ شراء والا مسئلہ ہے اور ماقبل میں گذر چکا ہے کہ شراء اور شفعہ میں کچھ منافات نہیں کیونکہ دونوں کا مال لینا ہے۔
The person for whom the option (khiyar) is stipulated in the sale, and he is also the shafi' (pre-emption right holder), then there is no pre-emption right for him because the sale is completed by his ratification. Contrary to the case where the option is for the buyer's side. Translation: Similarly, if a person becomes a guarantor for the seller for compensation and loss, and he is also the shafi', then there is no pre-emption right for him. Likewise, when the seller sold on behalf of another and stipulated an option, and the person for whom the option is stipulated ratified the sale, and he is also the shafi', then he will not receive pre-emption because the sale became final by his ratification. Contrary to the case where the option is for the buyer's side. Explanation: A buyer wants to purchase a house but has some hesitation that someone might claim a right or some other loss may occur. But Zaid becomes the guarantor for the seller and tells the buyer, 'Buy without worry; if any loss occurs, I will guarantee that the house will be handed over to you, or if I am unable to deliver, I will pay the price.' By chance, this Zaid is also the shafi' of the house. Then Zaid will not get pre-emption because the sale was completed by his side and he must uphold it. A person sold his house but stipulated an option for his friend Zaid, and Zaid ratified the sale. By chance, this Zaid is also the shafi' of the house. Then Zaid will not get pre-emption due to the same reason. Yes, if the buyer purchased a house and stipulated an option for Zaid, and Zaid ratified the purchase, and by chance Zaid is also the shafi', then in this case Zaid will get pre-emption because this is a case of purchase (shira'), and it has been stated earlier that there is no conflict between purchase and pre-emption because both involve taking ownership.
Source pages p. 110

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement from the Hanafi school concerning conditions that nullify the right of pre-emption (shuf'ah). The rule: if the shafi' himself is the one who completes the sale—either as a guarantor for the seller or as the person given the option to ratify the sale—he loses his right of pre-emption. The reasoning is that by ratifying the sale, he has effectively consented to the transaction, and it would be contradictory to then claim pre-emption to undo it. However, if the option is given to the shafi' on the buyer's side, meaning he is given the option to ratify the purchase, then his ratification does not destroy his right of pre-emption. This is explained through examples: if Zaid guarantees the seller that he will compensate the buyer for any loss, and Zaid is also the shafi', he loses his right because his guarantee effectively made the sale possible. Similarly, if the seller stipulates an option for Zaid to ratify the sale, and Zaid does so, he loses pre-emption. But if the buyer gives Zaid an option to ratify the purchase, and Zaid does so, he retains the right of pre-emption, because his act is one of buying (shira') not selling, and buying does not conflict with claiming pre-emption (which is also a kind of buying). The passage emphasizes that the decisive factor is whose side is being confirmed: the seller's side nullifies shuf'ah, the buyer's side does not.

Key Terms
الشفعة (al-shuf'ah): The right of a co-owner or neighbor to purchase the property that has been sold to a third party by substituting the buyer.
المشروط له الخيار (al-mashrut lahu al-khiyar): The person in whose favor an option (khiyar) has been stipulated in the contract.
ضامن (damin): A guarantor who takes responsibility for the seller's obligation to deliver the property or pay compensation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Zaid is the shafi' of a house. The seller stipulates an option for Zaid to ratify the sale. Zaid ratifies it. What is Zaid's right of pre-emption?
A) Zaid retains the right of pre-emption because he ratified the sale.
B) Zaid loses the right of pre-emption because his ratification completed the sale from the seller's side.
C) Zaid loses the right only if he guaranteed the seller's obligation.
D) Zaid retains the right if he was given the option by the buyer.

Key Takeaway
A shafi' loses his right of pre-emption when he ratifies the sale from the seller's side, whether as a guarantor or by exercising an option; however, ratifying from the buyer's side does not affect his right.

Buyu — Sales and Trade

Misinformation About Sale Price or Type of Consideration in Pre-emption
Explains rulings when shafi' is misinformed about the sale price or type of countervalue.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi ruling on pre-emption when the shafi' is misinformed about the sale price or the genus of the consideration, distinguishing between valid and invalid relinquishment.

Core Idea
A pre-emptor's relinquishment is invalid if misled about value or genus, unless the genus is the same in thamaniyya.

A pre-emptor (shafi') who is misinformed about the sale price or the type of countervalue (thaman) may later claim that his relinquishment of the right of pre-emption was based on incorrect information. The Hanafi school distinguishes between different scenarios: sometimes the relinquishment is invalid and the right remains, sometimes it is valid and the right is lost. The key factor is whether the actual consideration differs in genus from what was reported, and within that, whether the genus is considered united in terms of being a price (thamaniyya). This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah clarifies these distinctions and presents the dispute between the three imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) and Imam Zufar.

Guided Path
1
Identify the initial scenarios where reliquishment is invalid
The text gives two cases: (1) reported price higher than actual (e.g., told 1000 dirhams but actually 500), and (2) reported in dirhams but actual is measurable/weighable goods (like wheat) of equal value. In both, the shafi' did not know the true nature, so relinquishment is invalid.
The common factor is that the shafi' was misled about the difficulty of providing the countervalue.
2
Identify the scenario where reliquishment is valid
If the actual consideration is a commodity (non-measurable/weighable) of the same value, the relinquishment is valid because the obligation is the value (qimah), which remains unchanged.
This is because the shafi' understood the value, even if the form was different.
3
Understand the intra-Hanafi dispute on dinars vs dirhams
When the shafi' is told dirhams but the actual sale is in dinars of equal value, the three imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) rule that relinquishment is valid (no shuf'a), while Imam Zufar holds it is invalid (shuf'a remains).
The point of contention is whether dirhams and dinars are of the same genus (jins) in the context of pre-emption.
4
Analyze the proofs
The three imams analogize to zakat, where different currencies are combined, indicating unity of genus (thamaniyya). Zufar points to the permissibility of exchanging dirhams for dinars with profit, indicating different genera.
The Hanafi response is that thamaniyya overrides the exchange argument in the context of legal valuation.
5
Determine the mufta bihi position
The text clearly supports the three imams, stating 'لنا' and rejecting Zufar's view. The relied-upon position is that pre-emption is lost when the consideration is dinars worth the same as reported dirhams.
This is the operative ruling for fatwa in the Hanafi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الشفعة
اشرف الہدایہ شرح الاد و ہدایہ جلد-۱۳
تشریح شفیع کو کسی نے خبر دی کہ مکان ایک ہزار درہم میں فروخت ہوا ہے حالانکہ معاملہ ایسا نہیں بلکہ حقیقت میں بیچ ہوئی پانچ سو درہم میں اور پہلی خبر سن کر شفیع نے شمن کو زیادہ سمجھتے ہوئے شفعہ سے دست برداری دے دی تو اس کا شفعہ باطل نہ ہوگا۔ اور اگر اس کوخبر دی گئی کہ مکان ہزار درہم میں فروخت ہوا ہے حالانکہ وہ گیہوں یا جو یاکسی بھی میلی اور موزونی یا عددی متقارب کے بدلے میں فروخت ہوا ہے ہاں اس مکیلی یا موزونی یا عددی متقارب کی قیمت ہزار درہم ہیں اور شفیع نے پہلی خبر سن کر شفعہ سے دست برداری دے دی تھی اب معلوم ہوا کہ معاملہ یوں ہے تو بھی اس کی تسلیم باطل ہے اور اس کا حق شفعہ برقرار ہے۔ کیونکه و دسری صورت میں دست برداری کی وجہ یہ ہو سکتی ہے کہ ہزار درہم مہیا کرنا مشکل اور گیہوں اور جو وغیرہ دینا اس کیلئے آسان ہو۔ خصوصاً کا شتکاروں کیلئے روپے دینا قدرے بھاری اور غلہ دینا آسان ہوتا ہے اور چونکہ عددی متقارب مکیلی اور موزونی کے درجہ میں ہے لہذا اس کا بھی یہی حکم ہوگا ۔
مذکورہ مسئلہ کی مزید وضاحت
بخلاف ما اذا علم انها بيعت بعرض قيمته الف او اكثر لان الواجب فيه القيمة وهي دراهم اودنا نير وان بان آنها بیعت بدنانير قيمتها الف فلا شفعة له وكذا اذا كانت اكثر وقال زفر له الشفعة لاختلاف الجنس ولنا ان الجنس متحد فى حق الثمنية.
ترجمہ بخلاف اس صورت کے جبکہ شفیع کو ( ثانیا) معلوم ہوا کہ گھر فروخت ہوا ہے ایسے سامان کے بدلہ جس کی قیمت ہزار یا زیادہ ہے اسلئے کہ سامان میں قیمت واجب ہے اور قیمت یہی در اہم اور دنا نیر ہیں اور اگر یہ بات ظاہر ہوئی کہ مکان دنا نیر کے بدلے بیچا گیا ہے جس کی قیمت ہزار ہے تو شفیع کیلئے شفعہ نہیں ہے اور ایسے ہی جبکہ قیمت زیادہ ہو اور فرمایا ز فر نے کہ اس کیلئے شفعہ ہے جنس کے مختلف ہونے کی وجہ سے اور ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ ثمنیت کے حق میں جنس متحد ہے۔
تشریح شفیع کو اولاً معلوم ہوا کہ مکان ہزار میں فروخت ہوا ہے اور اس نے شفعہ سے دست برداری دے دی اب معلوم ہوا کہ وہ تو مکیلی اور موزونی کے علاوہ کسی اور سامان کے بدلہ فروخت ہوا ہے کہ اس سامان کی قیمت ہزار درہم یا زیادہ ہیں تو اب اس کی تسلیم درست ہے اور اب اس کو شفعہ نہیں ملے گا کیونکہ ہزار درہم اور وہ سامان جس کی قیمت ہزار درہم ہوں دونوں کا مال ایک ہے کیونکہ سامان کی صورت میں بھی یہاں قیمت ہی واجب ہوگی اور قیمت وہی ہے جو اس کو پہلے معلوم ہو چکی ہے یعنی ہزار درہم اور اگر شفیع کو اوالا معلوم ہوا کہ مکان ہزار درہم میں فروخت کیا گیا ہے تو اس نے شفعہ سے دست برداری دے دی۔ پھر ثانیا معلوم ہوا کہ مکان دنا نیر کے بدلہ فروخت ہوا ہے جن کی قیمت ہزار درہم یا زیادہ ہیں تو ائمہ ثلاثہ کے نزدیک شفعہ نہیں ملے گا۔ کیونکہ ثمنیت کے حق میں جنس متحد ہے اسی وجہ سے تو زکوۃ میں ایک کو دوسرے کی طرف ملالیا جاتا ہے۔ اور امام زفر فر ماتے ہیں کہ ان دونوں کے درمیان تفاضل اور کمی بیشی جائز ہے جو اختلاف جنس کی دلیل ہے اور مختلف الجنس کا حکم ماقبل میں آچکا ہے کہ اس سے شفعہ ساقط نہیں ہوتا مجمع الا نہر ص ۴۶۶ ج ۲ پر اس مسئلہ کو بسط سے بیان کیا گیا ہے ۔
The chapter of pre-emption. Explanation: If someone informed the pre-emptor that the house was sold for one thousand dirhams, but in reality it was sold for five hundred dirhams, and he gave up his right thinking the price was high, his pre-emption is not invalidated. And if he was informed that the house was sold for one thousand dirhams, but it was sold for wheat or barley or any measurable (makili) or weighable (mawzuni) or countable similar (adadi mutaqarib) items, and the value of those items is one thousand dirhams, and he gave up pre-emption based on the first news, his relinquishment is invalid and his right remains. The reason is that providing one thousand dirhams may be difficult while giving wheat/barley is easier, especially for farmers. Since countable items are analogous to measurable and weighable, the same ruling applies. Further clarification: Contrary to the case where he learns that it was sold for a commodity ('ard) whose value is one thousand or more, because the obligation is its value (qimah), which is dirhams or dinars. If it becomes clear that it was sold for dinars worth one thousand, then no pre-emption for him. Similarly if more. Zufar said he has pre-emption due to difference of genus. Our proof is that the genus is united in respect of being a price (thamaniyya). Explanation: If the pre-emptor initially learned that the house was sold for one thousand and he gave up, then learned that it was sold for a commodity other than makili or mawzuni whose value is one thousand or more, his relinquishment is valid and no pre-emption. Because one thousand dirhams and that commodity are the same in value. If he initially learned it was sold for one thousand dirhams and gave up, then learned it was sold for dinars worth one thousand or more, the three imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) say no pre-emption because the genus is united in respect of thamaniyya; for this reason in zakat one type is added to another. Imam Zufar held that exchange is permissible between them with difference, indicating difference of genus, and the ruling for different genus was given earlier that pre-emption is not lost. Ref: Majma' al-Anhar vol.2 p.466.
Source pages p. 111

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah addresses scenarios where the pre-emptor (shafi') is initially misinformed about the sale price or the type of consideration (thaman) and subsequently relinquishes his right of pre-emption (shuf'a). The ruling distinguishes between situations where the actual consideration differs in genus from what was reported. The text first presents two cases where the shafi''s relinquishment is invalid: (1) when the reported price is higher than the actual price (e.g., told 1000 dirhams but actual 500), and (2) when the reported price is in dirhams but the actual sale was for measurable/weighable goods (like wheat) of equal value. The rationale is that the difficulty of providing dirhams versus goods affects the decision. However, if the actual consideration is a commodity (not measurable/weighable) of the same value, the relinquishment is valid because the obligation is the value, which remains the same. A key point of ikhtilaf is when the actual consideration is dinars worth the same as the reported dirhams: the three imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) rule no shuf'a because dirhams and dinars share the same genus in terms of being a price (thamaniyya), analogizing to zakat where different coinages are combined. Imam Zufar disagrees, arguing that exchange with profit is allowed, indicating different genera. The Hanafi position is the majority view, supported by the analogy to zakat.

Key Terms
شفعة (shuf'a): The right of pre-emption, allowing a co-owner or neighbor to purchase a sold property by compelling the buyer to sell it to him.
شفيع (shafi'): The person entitled to pre-emption (the pre-emptor).
ثمن (thaman): The price or consideration exchanged for the property in a sale.
جنس (jins): Genus or category; in this context, the classification of the consideration (e.g., dirhams and dinars are considered the same jins in terms of being thaman).
ثمنية (thamaniyya): The quality or legal status of being a price (thaman). It is the basis for considering dirhams and dinars as the same genus.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the three imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad), what is the ruling if the pre-emptor is told the house was sold for 1000 dirhams, he relinquishes shuf'a, then learns it was actually sold for dinars worth 1000 dirhams?
A) He still has the right of pre-emption because the genus is different.
B) He has no pre-emption because the genus is united in thamaniyya.
C) He has no pre-emption only if the dinars are worth more than 1000 dirhams.
D) He has pre-emption only if he explicitly stated he would not accept dinars.

Key Takeaway
A pre-emptor's relinquishment is invalid if misled about the value or genus of the countervalue, unless the genus is the same in thamaniyya, in which case the right is lost.

Misinformation About Buyer and Extent of Sale in Pre-emption
Rulings on misinformation in pre-emption

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings for four scenarios of misinformation in shuf'a and identify the mufta bihi position in the intra-Hanafi dispute.

Core Idea
Misinformation about the buyer or sale extent can revive pre-emption, but whole-to-part misinformation does not (zahir al-riwayah).

This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah addresses cases where the pre-emptor (shafi') is misinformed about who bought the property or how much was sold. The rulings hinge on whether the relinquishment was based on a mistaken understanding of the buyer's identity or the extent of the sale. A key intra-Hanafi dispute arises when the shafi' is told the whole property was sold but later learns only part was sold. Understanding these scenarios is essential for correctly applying the rules of shuf'a.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four scenarios
List the four distinct cases presented: (1) buyer identity is wrong, (2) buyer is correct but with an additional co-buyer, (3) report of half sale but actual full sale, (4) report of full sale but actual half sale.
Cases 1-3 generally preserve shuf'a; case 4 has an ikhtilaf.
2
Analyze the basis for each ruling
For each scenario, determine why the relinquishment is considered invalid or valid. Key factors: jawaar (neighborly relations), darar al-shirkah (harm of partnership), and the principle of kull/ajza' (whole/parts).
3
Examine the intra-Hanafi dispute
For case 4 (whole reported, half sold), note that zahir al-riwayah denies shuf'a, while Abu Yusuf grants it. Understand the reasoning: relinquishment of the whole implies its parts vs. conditional relinquishment.
The text explicitly marks 'fi zahir al-riwayah' and then mentions Imam Abu Yusuf's view.
4
Apply the rulings to new scenarios
Given a new fact pattern, determine which scenario it matches and state the ruling, citing the relevant principle.

شفیع کو کہا کہ فلاں شخص مشتری ہے اس نے شفعہ چھوڑ دیا پھر معلوم ہوا کہ مشتری کوئی اور تو شفعہ کا حق ملے گا
كتاب الشفعة
قال واذا قيل له ان المشترى فلان فسلم الشفعة ثم علم ان غيره فله الشفعة لتفاوت الجوار ولو علم ان المشترى هو مع غيره فله ان ياخذ نصيب غيره لان التسليم لم يوجد فى حقه ولو بلغه شراء النصف فسلم ثم ظهر شراء الجميع فله الشفعة لان التسليم لضرر الشركة ولا شركة وفى عكسه لا شفعة في ظاهر الرواية لان التسليم فى الكل تسليم في ابعاضه.
ترجمہ امام قدوری نے فرمایا اور جبکہ کہا گیا شفیع سے کہ مشتری فلاں ہے تو اس نے شفعہ سے دست برداری دے دی پھر معلوم ہوا کہ مشتری اس کا غیر ہے تو اس کیلئے شفعہ ہے جوار کے متفاوت ہونے کی وجہ سے اور اگر یہ بات معلوم ہوئی کہ مشتری وہی ہے اپنے غیر کے ساتھ تو شفیع کیلئے حق ہے کہ اسکے غیر کے حصہ کو لے لے اسلئے کہ اس کے حق میں دست برداری نہیں پائی گئی ۔ اور اگر شفیع کوخبر پہنچی ہو نصف حصہ کے شراء کی تو اس نے دست برداری دے دی پھر پورے گھر کا شراء ظاہر ہوا تو اس کے لئے شفعہ ہے اس لئے کہ تسلیم شرکت کے ضرر کی وجہ تھی اور شرکت ہے نہیں اور اس کے عکس میں شفعہ نہیں ہے۔ ظاہر الروایہ کے مطابق اسلئے کہ کل میں دست برداری اس کے حصوں میں بھی دست برداری ہے۔
تشریح اگر شفیع کو اولاً معلوم ہوا کہ مشتری فلاں ہے جو اچھا آدمی ہے تو اس نے اپنا حق شفعہ چھوڑ دیا پھر معلوم ہوا کہ اس کو تو فلاں بد معاش نے خریدا ہے جو ہمیشہ مجھے پریشان کرتا رہے گا تو شفیع کو شفعہ ملے گا کیونکہ پڑوسی پڑوسی میں فرق ہوتا ہے جیسا کہ مشاہد ہے ۔ اور اگر اولاً معلوم ہوا کہ مشتری فلاں نیک ہے اور بعد میں پتہ چلا کہ فلاں بھی ہے اور اسکے ساتھ ایک اور ہے اور دونوں نے مل کر مکان خریدا ہے تو اب یہ حکم مکہ جس کے حق میں شفیع دست برداری دے چکا ہے اس کے علاوہ کے حصہ کو شفعہ میں لے سکتا ہے۔ اس لئے کہ اس کے حق میں دست برداری نہیں تھی۔ اگر شفیع کو معلوم ہوا کہ فلاں نے اپنا آدھا گھر فروخت کر دیا، تو شفیع نے شفعہ سے دست برداری دے دی اس نقصان کے پیش نظر کہ بائع کے ساتھ شرکت کا ضر ر سامنے آئے گا پھر اس کو دوبارہ معلوم ہوا کہ وہ خبر غلط تھی بلکہ بائع نے اپنا پورا امکان فروخت کیا ہے تو اس کا حق شفعہ برقرار ہے۔ کیونکہ یہاں شرکت کی بات نہیں اور اس کی تسلیم فقط ضر ر شرکت سے بچنے کیلئے تھی۔ اور اگر مسئلہ بر عکس ہو یعنی خبر ملی کہ فلاں نے اپنا پورا گھر فروخت کر دیا اور اس نے دست برداری دے دی پھر معلوم ہوا کہ بعض حصہ فروخت ہوا ہے تو اس کیلئے شفعہ نہیں ہے اور یہی ظاہر الروایہ ہے اسلئے کہ جب اس نے کل میں دست برداری ظاہر کر دی تو اس کے ابعاض وحصوں کے اندر بھی دست برداری ہوگی۔ البتہ امام ابو یوسف سے منقول ہے کہ اس صورت میں شفعہ ملے گا۔
Ashraf al-Hidayah Urdu commentary, vol. 13. The pre-emptor was told that so-and-so is the buyer, so he relinquished pre-emption, then he learned that the buyer was someone else: he has pre-emption due to difference in neighborly relations. And if he learned that the buyer is the same person together with another, he may take the share of the other, because relinquishment did not occur regarding him. And if he heard of the purchase of half and relinquished, then purchase of the whole appeared, he has pre-emption, because the relinquishment was due to harm of partnership, and there is no partnership. The opposite case: no pre-emption according to zahir al-riwayah, because relinquishment of the whole is relinquishment of its parts. Translation: Imam al-Quduri said: When it is said to him that the buyer is so-and-so, and he relinquished pre-emption, then he learned that it was someone else, he has pre-emption due to difference in neighborly relations. And if he learned that the buyer is the same together with another, he may take the share of the other, because relinquishment did not occur regarding him. And if news of purchase of half reached him and he relinquished, then purchase of the whole appeared, he has pre-emption, because the relinquishment was due to harm of partnership, and there is no partnership. The opposite case: no pre-emption according to zahir al-riwayah, because relinquishment of the whole is relinquishment of its parts. Explanation: If the pre-emptor initially learned that the buyer is so-and-so who is a good person, so he gave up his right, then learned that a bad neighbor bought it, he has pre-emption because neighbors differ. And if initially learned that the buyer is so-and-so good, then learned that another is with him and they jointly bought, he can take the share of the other besides the one regarding whom he relinquished. Because relinquishment did not occur regarding him. If the pre-emptor learned that someone sold half his house, and he gave up due to the harm of partnership, then learned the news was false and the seller sold the whole house, his right remains. Because there is no partnership and his relinquishment was only to avoid partnership harm. The opposite case: he was told that he sold his whole house and he gave up, then learned that only part was sold: no pre-emption according to zahir al-riwayah, because relinquishment of the whole includes its parts. However, Imam Abu Yusuf is reported to hold that pre-emption is granted in this case.
Source pages p. 112

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah discusses scenarios where the pre-emptor (shafi') is misinformed about the identity of the buyer (mushtari) or the extent of the sale, and his relinquishment of shuf'a based on that misinformation. The text, quoting Imam al-Quduri, presents several rulings: (1) If the shafi' is told that a specific person is the buyer and he relinquishes, but then learns that another person bought it, his pre-emption is revived because neighbors differ in character or relationship (jawaar) — e.g., a good neighbor vs a bad one. (2) If the buyer is the same person together with another, the shafi' may take only the other's share, as his relinquishment was only regarding the first. (3) If he hears that half was sold and relinquishes (to avoid partnership with the buyer), but learns the whole was sold, he retains shuf'a because the reason for relinquishment (harm of partnership) is absent. (4) The opposite: if he hears the whole was sold and relinquishes, then learns only part was sold, according to zahir al-riwaya he has no shuf'a because relinquishment of the whole implies relinquishment of its parts. However, Imam Abu Yusuf holds that he does have shuf'a in this case. The commentary explains each scenario with examples, emphasizing the role of intent and the harm of partnership.

Key Terms
جوار (jawaar): Neighborly relations; the character or quality of the neighbor's relationship with the pre-emptor.
تسلیم (tasleem): Relinquishment or surrender of the right of pre-emption explicitly or implicitly.
شرکت (shirkah): Partnership; in this context, the potential co-ownership resulting from buying a share of the property.
ظاہر الروایہ (zahir al-riwayah): The well-known and authoritative transmission from the early Hanafi masters, forming the relied-upon position.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to zahir al-riwayah, what is the ruling if the pre-emptor is told that the entire house was sold and he relinquishes shuf'a, but later learns that only half was sold?
A) He has shuf'a for the half that was sold.
B) He has no shuf'a because relinquishment of the whole includes its parts.
C) He has shuf'a only if the half is worth more than half of the reported price.
D) He has shuf'a only if he was unaware of the actual sale at the time of relinquishment.

Key Takeaway
In pre-emption, misinformation can revive the right only if it relates to the buyer's entire identity or if the sale extent was underreported; overreporting the sale extent (whole vs. part) does not revive shuf'a in the relied-upon Hanafi position.

Shuf'a Surrender Based on Mistaken Buyer Identity
Rulings on surrender of shuf'a when buyer identity is mistaken.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when a shafi' surrenders his right based on mistaken identity of the buyer, and distinguish between cases where the buyer is completely different vs. partially same.

Core Idea
Surrender of shuf'a based on false buyer identity does not bar the right.

In the Hanafi school, the right of preemption (shuf'a) can be surrendered, but the validity of that surrender depends on the accuracy of the information upon which it was based. This passage from al-Quduri's matn, as explained in al-Hidayah, clarifies two scenarios: when the shafi' is told the buyer is one person but it turns out to be another, and when the buyer is that person together with an additional buyer. Understanding these distinctions is essential for correctly applying the law of shuf'a in practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the initial report
What does the shafi' hear about the buyer? For example, 'the buyer is so-and-so' or 'the buyer is so-and-so and another.'
2
Note the shafi' action
The shafi' surrenders the shuf'a based on that initial report.
Surrender can be express or implied.
3
Identify the truth
What is the actual buyer? For example, it turns out to be a completely different person, or it is the same person along with another.
4
Apply the ruling
Determine if the surrender bars the right. If the buyer is completely different, the shafi' retains full shuf'a. If the buyer is the same plus another, the shafi' may take the share of the additional buyer.
The surrender is only with respect to the information provided.

Ashraf al-Hidayah, Urdu commentary on Hidayah, Volume 13. Book of Shuf'a. He said: And when it is said to him that the buyer is so-and-so, and he surrenders the shuf'a, then he learns that it is someone else, then he has the shuf'a due to difference of neighbor. And if he learns that the buyer is that person together with another, then he may take the share of the other because surrender has not occurred with respect to him. And if news of the purchase of half reaches him and he surrenders, then the purchase of the whole appears, then he has the shuf'a because the surrender was due to the harm of partnership, and there is no partnership. In its opposite, there is no shuf'a according to the apparent narration (Zahir al-Riwayah) because surrender in the whole is surrender in its parts. Translation: Imam al-Quduri said: And when the shafi' is told that the buyer is so-and-so, then he relinquishes the right of shuf'a, then it becomes known that the buyer is someone else, then he has the right of shuf'a due to the difference of neighbors. And if it becomes known that the buyer is that person along with another, then the shafi' has the right to take the share of the other because surrender did not occur with respect to him. And if news of the purchase of half reaches the shafi', and he relinquishes, then the purchase of the whole house becomes apparent, then he has the shuf'a because the surrender was due to the harm of partnership, and there is no partnership. In its opposite, there is no shuf'a according to Zahir al-Riwayah, because surrender in the whole is surrender in its parts. Commentary: If the shafi' first learns that the buyer is so-and-so who is a good person, then he relinquishes his right of shuf'a, then it becomes known that he was bought by so-and-so a bad person who will always trouble me, then the shafi' will get the shuf'a because neighbors differ, as is observed. And if first it becomes known that the buyer is so-and-so good, and later it is found that so-and-so is also there and with him another, and both together bought the house, then he can take the share other than the one for whom he surrendered, because surrender did not occur with respect to him. If the shafi' learns that so-and-so sold half his house, then the shafi' relinquishes shuf'a due to the harm of partnership with the seller, then he later learns that the news was wrong, rather the seller sold his entire property, then his right of shuf'a remains, because there is no partnership here, and his surrender was only to avoid the harm of partnership. And if the case is opposite, i.e., news comes that so-and-so sold his entire house and he relinquishes, then it becomes known that only a part was sold, then he has no shuf'a, and this is Zahir al-Riwayah, because when he shows surrender in the whole, it will also be surrender in its parts. However, it is narrated from Imam Abu Yusuf that in this case he will get the shuf'a.
Source pages p. 112

Commentary
This passage presents multiple rulings from Kitab al-Shuf'a. It is a ruling statement from the matn of al-Quduri (via Hidayah) followed by Urdu commentary. The first ruling: if the shafi' is told the buyer is a certain person and he surrenders his right, but then discovers the buyer is someone else, he retains the right of shuf'a because the identity of the neighbor matters (e.g., a good vs. bad neighbor). The second ruling: if the buyer is that person along with another, the shafi' may take the share of the other buyer because his surrender was only regarding the person originally mentioned. The third ruling: if he hears that half was sold and surrenders, then learns the whole was sold, he has shuf'a because his surrender was motivated by the harm of co-ownership, which does not exist in full sale. Conversely, if he hears the whole was sold and surrenders, then learns only part was sold, the relied-upon position (Zahir al-Riwayah) is that he has no shuf'a, since surrender in full implies surrender in part. However, Imam Abu Yusuf disagrees, holding that he does have shuf'a. The commentary clarifies each scenario with practical examples. The passage does not cite external proofs but relies on legal reasoning (ta'lil).

Key Terms
شفعة (shuf'a): The right of preemption in property adjacent to the shafi'.
تسليم (taslim): Surrender or relinquishment of the right of shuf'a.
جوار (jīwār): Neighborly proximity; the basis for shuf'a for a non-sharīk neighbor.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If the shafi' surrenders after being told the buyer is X, then discovers the buyer is X and Y together, what is his right?
A) He loses completely.
B) He may take X's share only.
C) He may take Y's share.
D) The sale is void.

Key Takeaway
Surrender of shuf'a based on mistaken buyer identity does not extinguish the right; the shafi' retains it in the situations described.

Shuf'a Surrender Based on Mistaken Sale Extent (Half vs. Full)
Rulings on surrender of shuf'a when the extent of sale is mistaken.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the ruling for the case where a shafi' surrenders after hearing of a half sale then discovers a full sale, and the opposite case, including the intra-Hanafi difference.

Core Idea
Surrender based on half-then-full revives the right; full-then-half extinguishes it (in the relied-upon view).

The second part of the passage deals with mistakes regarding the quantity of the property sold. The shafi' may hear that half was sold and surrender, then learn that the whole was actually sold. Conversely, he may hear of a whole sale and surrender, then discover only part was sold. The Hanafi ruling differs in these two cases, and there is a notable difference of opinion between the school's relied-upon position (Zahir al-Riwayah) and Imam Abu Yusuf on the second case. Understanding the reasoning behind this distinction is key to mastering the law of shuf'a.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two sub-scenarios
Case A: shafi' hears of half sale and surrenders, then discovers full sale (half-to-full). Case B: shafi' hears of full sale and surrenders, then discovers half sale (full-to-half).
2
Analyze the reasoning for half-to-full
The surrender was motivated by the desire to avoid the harm of partnership (co-ownership). Since full sale does not create partnership (the buyer owns the whole), that reason no longer applies, so the surrender is invalid and the right revives.
Key phrase: 'lianna al-taslīm li-darar al-shirkah wa lā shirkah'.
3
Analyze the opposite case (full-to-half)
The surrender was for the whole sale. Since the whole includes the part, surrendering the whole implies surrendering every part. Therefore, when only part is sold, the shafi' cannot reclaim the right for that part.
Key phrase: 'al-taslīm fī al-kulli taslīm fī ab'ādihi'.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Imam Abu Yusuf disagrees: he holds that the shafi' still has shuf'a for the half, because the surrender was specifically for the whole, not the part. The relied-upon position is Zahir al-Riwayah.
The text says 'fī zāhir al-riwāyah' indicating the preferred transmission.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

قال واذا قيل له ان المشترى فلان فسلم الشفعة ثم علم ان غيره فله الشفعة لتفاوت الجوار ولو علم ان المشترى هو مع غيره فله ان ياخذ نصيب غيره لان التسليم لم يوجد فى حقه ولو بلغه شراء النصف فسلم ثم ظهر شراء کہ تسلیم شرکت کے ضرر کی وجہ تھی اور شرکت ہے نہیں اور اس کے عکس میں شفعہ نہیں ہے۔ ظاہر الروایہ کے مطابق اسلئے کہ کل میں دست برداری اس کے حصوں میں بھی دست برداری ہے۔ تشریح اگر شفیع کو اولاً معلوم ہوا کہ ہے جیسا کہ مشاہد ہے ۔ اور اگر اولاً معلوم ہوا کہ مشتری فلاں نیک ہے اور بعد میں پتہ چلا کہ فلاں بھی ہے اور اسکے ساتھ ایک اور ہے اور دونوں نے مل کر مکان خریدا ہے تو اب یہ حکم مکہ جس کے حق میں شفیع دست کیلئے شفعہ نہیں ہے اور یہی ظاہر الروایہ ہے اسلئے کہ جب اس نے کل میں دست برداری ظاہر کر دی تو اس کے ابعاض وحصوں کے اندر بھی دست برداری ہوگی۔ البتہ امام ابو یوسف سے منقول ہے کہ اس صورت میں شفعہ ملے گا۔
Ashraf al-Hidayah, Urdu commentary on Hidayah, Volume 13. Book of Shuf'a. He said: And when it is said to him that the buyer is so-and-so, and he surrenders the shuf'a, then he learns that it is someone else, then he has the shuf'a due to difference of neighbor. And if he learns that the buyer is that person together with another, then he may take the share of the other because surrender has not occurred with respect to him. And if news of the purchase of half reaches him and he surrenders, then the purchase of the whole appears, then he has the shuf'a because the surrender was due to the harm of partnership, and there is no partnership. In its opposite, there is no shuf'a according to the apparent narration (Zahir al-Riwayah) because surrender in the whole is surrender in its parts. Translation: Imam al-Quduri said: And when the shafi' is told that the buyer is so-and-so, then he relinquishes the right of shuf'a, then it becomes known that the buyer is someone else, then he has the right of shuf'a due to the difference of neighbors. And if it becomes known that the buyer is that person along with another, then the shafi' has the right to take the share of the other because surrender did not occur with respect to him. And if news of the purchase of half reaches the shafi', and he relinquishes, then the purchase of the whole house becomes apparent, then he has the shuf'a because the surrender was due to the harm of partnership, and there is no partnership. In its opposite, there is no shuf'a according to Zahir al-Riwayah, because surrender in the whole is surrender in its parts. Commentary: If the shafi' first learns that the buyer is so-and-so who is a good person, then he relinquishes his right of shuf'a, then it becomes known that he was bought by so-and-so a bad person who will always trouble me, then the shafi' will get the shuf'a because neighbors differ, as is observed. And if first it becomes known that the buyer is so-and-so good, and later it is found that so-and-so is also there and with him another, and both together bought the house, then he can take the share other than the one for whom he surrendered, because surrender did not occur with respect to him. If the shafi' learns that so-and-so sold half his house, then the shafi' relinquishes shuf'a due to the harm of partnership with the seller, then he later learns that the news was wrong, rather the seller sold his entire property, then his right of shuf'a remains, because there is no partnership here, and his surrender was only to avoid the harm of partnership. And if the case is opposite, i.e., news comes that so-and-so sold his entire house and he relinquishes, then it becomes known that only a part was sold, then he has no shuf'a, and this is Zahir al-Riwayah, because when he shows surrender in the whole, it will also be surrender in its parts. However, it is narrated from Imam Abu Yusuf that in this case he will get the shuf'a.
Source pages p. 112

Commentary
This passage presents multiple rulings from Kitab al-Shuf'a. It is a ruling statement from the matn of al-Quduri (via Hidayah) followed by Urdu commentary. The first ruling: if the shafi' is told the buyer is a certain person and he surrenders his right, but then discovers the buyer is someone else, he retains the right of shuf'a because the identity of the neighbor matters (e.g., a good vs. bad neighbor). The second ruling: if the buyer is that person along with another, the shafi' may take the share of the other buyer because his surrender was only regarding the person originally mentioned. The third ruling: if he hears that half was sold and surrenders, then learns the whole was sold, he has shuf'a because his surrender was motivated by the harm of co-ownership, which does not exist in full sale. Conversely, if he hears the whole was sold and surrenders, then learns only part was sold, the relied-upon position (Zahir al-Riwayah) is that he has no shuf'a, since surrender in full implies surrender in part. However, Imam Abu Yusuf disagrees, holding that he does have shuf'a. The commentary clarifies each scenario with practical examples. The passage does not cite external proofs but relies on legal reasoning (ta'lil).

Key Terms
شفعة (shuf'a): The right of preemption in property adjacent to the shafi'.
تسليم (taslim): Surrender or relinquishment of the right of shuf'a.
جوار (jīwār): Neighborly proximity; the basis for shuf'a for a non-sharīk neighbor.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a shafi' surrenders after hearing of a full sale, then discovers only half was sold, what is the ruling according to the relied-upon view?
A) He has shuf'a for the half.
B) He has no shuf'a.
C) He must wait for a court decision.
D) The sale is void.

Key Takeaway
Surrender based on mistaken extent is not binding if the mistake is from half to full (right remains), but it is binding if from full to half (right lost in the relied-upon view).

The Lawful Trick to Drop Shuf'a by Excluding One Cubit
Presents a lawful stratagem to nullify shuf'a.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi hila to nullify shuf'a by retaining or gifting one cubit adjacent to the shafi', and state the legal reasoning based on contiguity and co-ownership.

Core Idea
Retaining or gifting one cubit adjacent to the shafi' severs contiguity, thereby nullifying shuf'a.

This passage from the Hidayah presents a permissible legal stratagem (hila) to avoid the right of shuf'a when the neighbor (shafi') is harmful. The trick relies on breaking the condition of adjacency (ittisāl) or on the principle that a co-owner (sharik) takes precedence over a neighbor (jar). Understanding this ruling illustrates how Hanafi law balances rights with practical necessity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is selling a house while excluding one cubit on the side adjacent to the shafi'. The ruling: no shuf'a for the shafi'.
2
Understand the condition for shuf'a
Shuf'a requires physical contiguity between the shafi's property and the sold property. If contiguity is broken, the right falls.
3
Analyze the two versions of the hila
Version A: seller retains the one cubit (does not sell it). Version B: seller gifts that cubit to the buyer first. In both, the sold part is not adjacent to the shafi.
4
Note the alternative legal basis for the gift version
When the buyer receives the gifted cubit, he becomes a co-owner (sharik). Later sale of the rest gives the buyer priority as sharik over the jar.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الشفعة
۱۱۲
اشرف البدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد ۱۳
ـصل
ترجمہ فصل ہے اسقاط شفعہ کے حیلوں کے بیان میں
بائع ایک گز کی بقدر جگہ جو شفیع سے ملی ہوئی ہے نہ بیچے تو شفیع کو شفعہ کاحق نہیں
قال و اذا باع دارا الا مقدار ذراع منها فى طول الحد الذى يلى الشفيع فلا شفعة له لانقطاع الجوار وهذه حيلة وكذا اذا وهب منه هذا المقدار و سلّمه اليه لما بينا
ترجمہ امام قدوری نے کہا اور جبکہ بیچ دیا گھر کو مگر اس میں سے ایک ذراع کی مقدار کو اس پٹی کے طول میں جو شفیع سے ملی ہوئی ہے تو اس کیلئے شفعہ نہ ہوگا جوار کے منقطع ہو جانے کی وجہ سے اور یہ ایک حیلہ ہے ( اسقاط شفعہ کا ) اور ایسے ہی جبکہ اس مقدار کو مشتری ہبہ کر چکا ہو اور اس مقدار کو مشتری کے سپرد کر دیا ہو اس دلیل کی وجہ سے جس کو ہم بیان کر چکے ہیں۔

جائے گا۔ مثلاً بائع اور مشتری جس گھر کو بچنا چاہتے ہیں اس کے جوار میں بہت شریر آدمی آباد ہے اگر اس نے شفعہ کا دعوی کر دیا تو تمام پڑوسیوں کو تکلیف پہنچائے گا تو بائع کو چاہئے کہ اپنا سارا گھر مشتری کو فروخت کر دئے۔ مگر جس جانب سے وہ مکان شفیع کے مکان سے ملا ہوا ہے ادھر سے پوری پٹی ایک ہاتھ کے بقدر چھوڑ دے یعنی اس کو فروخت نہ کرے تو اب وہ جار گھر کے اندر شفعہ کا مستحق نہ ہوگا۔ کیونکہ جتنا حصہ فروخت ہوا ہے اس حصہ کا اس کی ملکیت سے اتصال نہیں ہے۔

Book of Shuf'a. 112. Ashraf al-Bidaya, Urdu commentary on Hidayah, Volume 13. Chapter. Translation: This is a chapter on tricks to drop shuf'a. The seller does not sell a piece of land measuring one cubit adjacent to the shafi', then the shafi' has no right of shuf'a. He said: And when he sells a house except the amount of one cubit in the length of the boundary that is adjacent to the shafi', then there is no shuf'a for him due to the severance of adjacency, and this is a trick. Similarly, when he gifts this amount to him and delivers it to him, for the reason we have explained. Translation: Imam al-Quduri said: And when he sells the house but excludes an amount of one cubit in the length of the strip that is adjacent to the shafi', then there is no shuf'a for him due to the severance of adjacency, and this is a trick (to drop shuf'a). And similarly, when he gifts this amount to the buyer and delivers it to him, for the reason we have explained. Commentary: Sometimes the shafi' is so malicious and immoral that causing trouble to people is his known behavior; if there were no way to be free from him, certain harm would occur. So in this chapter, some tricks and measures are mentioned by which the right of shuf'a is annulled. For example, the seller and buyer of a house have a very wicked person living nearby; if he claims shuf'a, he will trouble all neighbors. So the seller should sell his entire house to the buyer, but on the side where the house is adjacent to the shafi's house, he leaves an entire strip of one cubit, i.e., does not sell it. Then that neighbor will not be entitled to shuf'a in the house because the sold portion has no contiguity with his property. And when the seller later sells the remainder to the buyer, still the shafi' will not get shuf'a, because the shafi' is merely a neighbor, while the buyer is a co-owner, and it has passed earlier that the co-owner takes precedence over the neighbor. Similarly, if the seller gifts the abovementioned amount to the buyer and hands it over to him, then shuf'a does not apply to a gift, and there is no contiguity; then when he sells the remainder to the buyer, the shafi' will not get shuf'a because the co-owner takes precedence over the neighbor.
Source pages p. 113

Commentary
This passage presents a lawful hila (trick) to circumvent a shafi's right of preemption. It is a ruling statement from the matn followed by Urdu commentary. The matn states that if the seller sells the entire house except for one cubit on the side adjacent to the shafi', the shafi' loses his right because the sold portion is not contiguous to his property. This is a permissible stratagem to avoid the harm of a bad neighbor. The commentary explains the reasoning: the shafi' is only a neighbor (jar), not a co-owner (sharik). Once the buyer becomes a co-owner by owning part of the property (through the gift or retained portion), when the rest is sold, the buyer as co-owner has superior right over the neighbor. The same applies if the seller gifts that one cubit to the buyer first, then sells the rest; the buyer's co-ownership blocks the neighbor's shuf'a. The passage also notes that this is a well-known principle: a sharik is preferred over a jar.

Key Terms
حيلة (hila): A lawful stratagem or legal trick to achieve a permissible end, here dropping shuf'a.
ذراع (dhirā'): A cubit, a unit of length used as a minimum measure to break contiguity.
اتصال (ittisāl): Contiguity or physical junction between the shafi's property and the sold property.

Key Terms from Source Passage

What is the condition for the trick to drop shuf'a by selling except one cubit?
A) The one cubit must be sold to a third party.
B) The one cubit must be retained by the seller or gifted to the buyer first.
C) The shafi' must consent.
D) The property must be agricultural land.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits using a lawful trick (hila) by excluding one cubit adjacent to the shafi' to drop shuf'a, based on severance of contiguity or co-ownership precedence.

Ruling on Shuf'a When Buyer Purchases Shares Sequentially
States that if a buyer buys one share first and then the rest, the neighbor has shuf'a only in the first share.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the neighbor's right of shuf'a is restricted to the first share in a sequential purchase and identify the legal reasoning based on the Hanafi hierarchy of preemption rights.

Core Idea
In sequential purchases, the first share triggers shuf'a for the neighbor; the second does not because the buyer becomes a co-owner.

This lesson examines a specific scenario in property preemption (shuf'a) where a buyer purchases shares of a house in separate transactions. The Hanafi school holds that the neighbor's right of preemption applies only to the first share, because by the second purchase the buyer becomes a co-owner, and a co-owner's right to retain the property takes precedence over a neighbor's right. This ruling illustrates the Hanafi prioritization among parties entitled to shuf'a.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two roles in the scenario
Distinguish between the 'neighbor' (jār) - a person with adjacent property not a co-owner, and the 'co-owner' (sharīk) - a person who acquires a share in the same property. In the first purchase, the buyer is a stranger to the property, so the neighbor is the only potential claimant. In the second purchase, the buyer becomes a sharīk.
The Hanafi school grants shuf'a to both co-owners and neighbors, but co-owners have priority.
2
State the ruling for each share
Read the passage: the neighbor has the right of shuf'a in the first share but not in the second. Summarize this as a clear ruling.
This is the ḥukm derived from the matn.
3
Explain the rationale
The text provides the reason: 'because the shafi' is a neighbor in both, but the buyer in the second is a co-owner, so he takes precedence.' Understand that the buyer's status changes, and a co-owner's right in shuf'a is stronger than a neighbor's when both exist.
This demonstrates the hierarchy: sharīk > jār in preemption.
4
Analyze the hīla (legal trick)
The passage mentions that if the buyer wants to employ a trick, he buys the first share at a low price and the rest at a higher price. This does not change the shuf'a ruling but affects the price the neighbor must pay if he exercises his right in the first share.
The hīla is a way to minimize loss while staying within the law.
5
Apply to a similar scenario
Consider a case where a buyer purchases a 1/3 share on Monday and the remaining 2/3 on Friday. The neighbor's shuf'a exists only for the 1/3 share purchased on Monday, because after that purchase, the buyer becomes a co-owner before buying the rest.
The sequence of transactions matters; simultaneous purchase would yield a different outcome.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مشتری نے گھر کا ایک حصہ خرید امن کے بدلے پھر گھر کا دوسرا حصہ بھی خرید لیا تو شفیع کو پہلے حصہ میں تو صرف حق شفعہ حاصل ہوگا
قال واذا ابتاع منها سهما بثمن ثم ابتاع بقيتها فالشفعة للجار فى السهم الاول دون الثاني لان الشفيع جار فيهما الا ان المشترى فى الثانى شريك فيتقدم عليه فان اراد الحيلة ابتاع السهم بالثمن الادرهما مثلا والباقي بالباقي
The buyer bought one share of the house for a price, then bought the other share of the house as well. Then the shafi' will only have the right of shuf'a in the first share. He said: And when he buys from it a share for a price, then buys the rest of it, then the shuf'a belongs to the neighbor in the first share but not the second, because the shafi' is a neighbor in both, but the buyer in the second is a co-owner, so he takes precedence. And if he wants the trick, he buys the first share for the lesser price, for example, and the rest for the remaining.
Source pages p. 113

Commentary
This passage provides a ruling on shuf'a when a buyer purchases parts of a property in separate transactions. The matn from al-Quduri (via Hidayah) states: if someone buys a share first, then later buys the remainder, the neighbor (jar) has shuf'a only in the first share, not in the second. The reason is that by the second purchase, the buyer becomes a co-owner (sharik) with the neighbor, and a co-owner's right to retain property takes precedence over a neighbor's right of preemption. The commentary adds that if a trick (hila) is desired, the buyer can purchase the first share at a very low price and the rest at a slightly higher price, but the principle remains. This ruling illustrates the Hanafi prioritization: a co-owner's right in shuf'a is stronger than a neighbor's right.

Key Terms
سهم (sahm): A share or portion of a property; unit of ownership.
جار (jār): Neighbor, a person with adjacent property but not a co-owner.
شريك (sharīk): Co-owner, partner in ownership.
حيلة (hīla): A strategy to achieve a legal outcome without violating the law; here, a trick to minimize the neighbor's shuf'a right.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the scenario of sequential purchases, why does the neighbor lose shuf'a in the second share?
A) Because the neighbor waived his right.
B) Because the buyer becomes a co-owner and takes precedence over a neighbor.
C) Because the property is divided.
D) Because the second purchase was a gift.

Key Takeaway
The neighbor's shuf'a right is limited to the first share in a sequential purchase because the buyer becomes a co-owner with higher priority in subsequent shares.

Hila in Shuf'a: Protecting the Seller from Loss on Istihqaq
Explaining a preferred legal device using sarf conditions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to compare two Hanafi legal devices to protect the seller in shuf'a and identify the operative condition (qabd in sarf) that determines the validity of the second hila.

Core Idea
A valid hila must not shift loss to the seller; the sarf-based hila uses the invalidity of deferred possession to limit liability.

In Hanafi law, when a property sold is later reclaimed by its rightful owner, the buyer recovers the price from the seller. If the price is high, the seller suffers a great loss. The commentators of Al-Hidayah present two hila to mitigate this risk. This lesson examines both devices, focusing on the mechanics of the second, preferred hila involving a sarf transaction, and highlights the crucial condition of immediate possession (qabd) in money exchange.

Guided Path
1
Identify the problem
Understand why the seller faces potential loss: the house is reclaimed, the buyer takes back the price, and if the price was high, the seller loses the difference.
2
First hila: the cloth scenario
Analyze the hila where part of the price is disguised as a separate cloth sale. Identify its vulnerability: if the house is reclaimed, the cloth sale remains valid, so the seller must return the full cash price, suffering loss.
3
Second hila: the dirham-dinar exchange
Examine how the seller sells the house for a moderate sum (1000 dirhams) and then exchanges those dirhams for a dinar via a sarf contract. Understand that if the house is reclaimed, the sarf contract becomes void due to non-possession of the dirhams (they were still a debt).
The condition of qabd in sarf: immediate possession before separation is a condition for validity.
4
Compare the two devices
Determine why the second hila is superior: it limits the seller's liability to only the dinar, avoiding the full loss of the price.
5
Reflect on the role of sarf conditions
Note that the invalidity of the sarf contract arises from the missing qabd, which is a deliberate defect. The seller intentionally fails to take possession of the dirhams, causing the contract to be void, so only the actual property (dinar) needs to be returned.

Source Text

Pre-emption. 114. Ashraf al-Bidaya sharh Urdu Hidaya volume 13. Translation: But the matter is that if the property subject to pre-emption is proven to be rightfully owned by another, then the full price remains upon the buyer (seller) because the second sale remains valid, so harm will befall the seller. And the better view is that in exchange for those dirhams which are the price, one dinar should be sold, so that when the house subject to pre-emption is proven to be rightfully owned by another, the sale of sarf becomes void, and only returning the one dinar becomes obligatory, not anything else. Elucidation: The author of al-Hidayah says that the aforementioned hila involving cloth is very good, but it has one defect: if by chance someone claims right of ownership over this house and the judge gives the house to the rightful owner, then the house that was in the buyer's possession is gone, so the buyer will take back his price from the seller. Now the question arises: will he take back the original price (one thousand) or the cloth? He said: he will take back the price of the house, and the price is one thousand. As for the cloth matter, that is a separate contract which has not ended; rather it is the first contract in which the price was set at twenty thousand. So the seller will have to pay the full price, and this is a great loss for the seller because he took cloth and must pay one thousand. So this hila was good, but it carries the risk of this loss for the seller. Therefore the better form is that he sells the house for one thousand dirhams, and due to the difference in genus between dirhams and dinars, excess and deficiency are allowed, so then he sells one dinar in exchange for one thousand dirhams, and this is a sale of sarf. Now listen: if the pre-emptor wants to take, he will take in exchange for one thousand; and if by chance the house is proven to be rightfully owned by another, the seller only has to return one dinar. Because the event shows that no price is owed by the buyer. So the return of the full price is not obligatory. Now remains the matter of the sale of sarf: the sale of sarf occurred between one thousand and one dinar, that one thousand which was owed by the buyer, i.e. the seller gives to the buyer and the buyer gives one dinar to the seller. However, in a sale of sarf, possession of the price before separation of the parties is a condition, and possession did not occur here; rather the twenty thousand were still owed by the buyer, not paid. So in any case the sale of sarf became void. And in the first scenario, the sale of cloth remained valid; and when the sale of sarf became void, now the seller only has to return that which he has, which is one dinar. Thus the snake is killed and the stick is not broken, meaning protection from the harm of the pre-emptor was achieved and the seller's harm was also removed. Warning: The commentators have transmitted a case from Qadi Khan and explained it, but that case does not connect with the author's text. In Fath al-Qadir volume 4, page 449, he has mentioned this case and clarified this non-correspondence, and has briefly transmitted the discussion of the issue as we have written it.
Source pages p. 115

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (sharh) on a discussion in Al-Hidayah regarding a legal device (hila) used in shuf'a (pre-emption) to protect the seller from loss if the sold property is later discovered to belong to someone else (istihqaq). The problem arises when a property is sold with a high price (e.g., 20,000 dirhams) but the actual transaction is structured with a separate exchange of cloth to reduce the price. If the property is reclaimed by its rightful owner, the buyer recovers his price from the seller. If the price was high, the seller suffers a huge loss. The first hila involved selling cloth separately, but if the house is reclaimed, the buyer takes back the full original price (20,000) because the cloth sale is a separate contract that remains valid, and the seller is left with only the cloth. This is a loss for the seller. A better hila is to sell the house for a moderate sum (1,000 dirhams) and then immediately sell those dirhams for a dinar (sarf transaction). If the house is reclaimed, the seller only returns the dinar because the sarf transaction is considered void (due to lack of possession, qabd, before separation). Thus the seller loses only the dinar, not the full 1,000 dirhams. The commentator explains that the sarf contract is invalid because possession of the price was not taken before the parties separated. The first hila with cloth is also valid but carries risk. The passage concludes that this second hila achieves both objectives: protecting the pre-emptor's right and preventing loss to the seller. A note warns that some commentators have added a case from Qadi Khan that does not align with the text, and the correct view is as presented.

Key Terms
شفعة (shuf'a): Pre-emption: the right of a co-owner or neighbor to purchase property sold to a third party under certain conditions.
حیلہ (hila): A legal device or stratagem used to achieve a permissible result while technically fulfilling the letter of the law.
بیع صرف (bay' al-sarf): The sale of gold for gold, silver for silver, or gold for silver, with specific conditions of possession (qabd) and equality in quantity for same genus.
قبض (qabd): Taking possession; physical or constructive receipt of the object of sale.
مستحق (mustahaqq): Rightful owner; one who is legally entitled to the property.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because the price was not specified correctly.
B) Because possession (qabd) was not taken before the parties separated.
C) Because the buyer did not consent.
D) Because the house was reclaimed.

Key Takeaway
The sarf-based hila effectively protects the seller from loss upon istihqaq by exploiting the condition that a sarf contract without immediate possession is void.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Legal Stratagems to Drop Shuf'a and Zakat
Intra-Hanafi dispute on hila to drop shuf'a and zakat

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the differing positions of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad on the ruling of hila for dropping shuf'a and zakat, and identify the operative fatwa (mufta bihi) according to later Hanafi authorities.

Core Idea
Preventing a right from arising is not harm — Abu Yusuf; defeating the law's purpose is harm — Muhammad.

This lesson examines an intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad on the ruling of using legal stratagems (hila) to prevent the right of pre-emption (shuf'a) or zakat from becoming established. The core question is whether such a stratagem is permissible or disliked, and the reasoning turns on whether preventing a right from arising constitutes harm. Understanding this dispute clarifies the Hanafi approach to hiyal and the importance of timing in determining legal rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the two positions
State clearly what legal stratagem is being considered (preventing shuf'a or zakat from becoming due) and the two rulings: Abu Yusuf says it is not disliked (mubah); Muhammad says it is disliked (makruh tanzihi).
2
Understand each imam's reasoning
Analyze the rationale: Muhammad argues that shuf'a is legislated to remove harm, so allowing a stratagem that prevents harm removal defeats the law's purpose. Abu Yusuf counters that since the right has not yet been established, preventing its occurrence is not an act of harm.
The dispute is based on the definition of 'harm' and the scope of legal causation.
3
Note the practical difference and later tarjih
Recognize that the mufta bihi depends on timing: before the right arises, Abu Yusuf's view is followed; after the right arises, it is unanimously disliked. Also note the author's preference to differentiate between shuf'a and zakat.
Majma' al-Anhur and Ashraf al-Hidaya provide the tarjih.
4
Distinguish between shuf'a and zakat according to the author
The author of Ashraf al-Hidaya holds that for shuf'a, the stratagem is not disliked even after establishment? Actually, he says for shuf'a it is not disliked, but for zakat it is disliked. This nuance is part of the later preferred view.
Check the exact statement: 'mujtaba' (preferred) in the author's own words.

قال ولا تكره الحيلة فى اسقاط الشفعة عند ابي يوسف وتكره عند محمد لان الشفعة انما وجبت لدفع الضرر ولو ابحنا الحيلة ما دفعناه ولا بى يوسف انه منع عن اثبات الحق فلا يعد ضررا وعلى هذا الخلاف الحيلة في اسقاط الزكوة .
ترجمہ قدوری نے فرمایا اور ا بو یوسف کے نزدیک اسقاط شفعہ میں حیلہ مکروہ نہیں ہے اور محمد کے نزدیک مکروہ ہے اسلئے شفعہ ثابت ہوتا ہے ضرور کو دور کرنے کیلئے اور اگر ہم حیلہ کو جائز کر دیں تو ہم ضر ر کو دور نہیں کر سکیں گے۔ اورانا بو یوسف کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ یہ تو اثبات روکنا ہے حق سے تو اس کو ضر ر شمار نہیں کیا جائے گا اور اسی اختلاف پر اسقاط زکوۃ کا حیلہ ہے۔
تشریح حیلہ کو اختیار کرنا کیسا ہے اس میں امام ابو یوسف اور امام محمد کا اختلاف ہے۔ امام محمد نے اس کو مکروہ کہا ہے اور امام ابو یوسف نے بلا کراہت جائز کہا ہے۔
امام محمد فرماتے ہیں کہ شفعہ کا ثبوت اسلئے ہوا کہ شفیع کا ضرر دور ہوا اگر ہم حیلے اختیار کر کے اس حق کو ساقط کریں گے تو گویا ہم نے لوگوں کا ضرر دور نہیں کیا اس وجہ سے یہ فعل مکروہ ہے۔ امام ابو یوسف فرماتے ہیں کہ اگر شفیع کا حق ثابت ہو جا تا اور پھر اس کو دور کیا جاتا جب ہی تو شفیع کا ضر شمار کیا جاتا اور یہاں ابھی تک شفیع کا حق ہی ثابت نہ ہوا تھا کہ اس کے ثابت ہونے کے امکان کوشتم کر دیا تو یہ ضر ر اور ظلم کیسے ہوگا۔ زکوۃ کے اسقاط میں حیلہ اختیار کرنے میں بھی یہی اختلاف ہے۔ امام ابو یوسف کے نزدیک مکروہ نہیں ہے اور امام محمد کے نزدیک مکروہ ہے۔ مجمع الا نہر ص ۴۶۷ ج ۲ پر ہے کہ ثبوت شفعہ سے پہلے حیلہ کرنے میں ابو یوسف کے قول پر فتویٰ ہے اور ثبوت کے بعد بالا جماع مکروہ ہے پھر کہا ہے کہ میرے نزدیک مختار یہ ہے کہ شفعہ کے اندر حیلہ مکروہ نہیں ہے اور زکوۃ کے اندر مکروہ ہے۔

جواب سلب الانہر ص ۴۱۶ ج ۲ پر ہے:
ولا حيلة لاسقاط الحيلة وقد طلبناها كثيراً فلم نجدها
He said: The legal stratagem to drop the right of pre-emption is not disliked according to Abu Yusuf, and it is disliked according to Muhammad. Because the right of pre-emption is established to repel harm, and if we permit the stratagem, we have not repelled it. And for Abu Yusuf: because it is preventing the establishment of the right, so it is not considered harm. And upon this difference is the stratagem to drop zakat. Translation: Al-Quduri said: According to Abu Yusuf, the stratagem to drop pre-emption is not disliked, and according to Muhammad it is disliked because pre-emption is established to remove harm, and if we permit the stratagem, we cannot remove harm. And Abu Yusuf's argument is that it is preventing the establishment of the right, so it is not counted as harm. And upon this difference is the stratagem to drop zakat. Explanation: The ruling on adopting a stratagem is disputed between Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad. Imam Muhammad said it is disliked, and Imam Abu Yusuf said it is permissible without dislike. Imam Muhammad says pre-emption was established to remove harm from the pre-emptor; if we adopt stratagems to drop this right, we have not removed harm, so the act is disliked. Imam Abu Yusuf says that if the pre-emptor's right had been established and then removed, then harm would be considered, but here the right has not yet been established; the possibility of its establishment is destroyed, so how can this be harm or injustice? The same difference applies to the stratagem to drop zakat. According to Imam Abu Yusuf it is not disliked, and according to Imam Muhammad it is disliked. In Majma' al-Anhur, vol. 2, p. 467, it states that before the establishment of pre-emption, the fatwa is on Abu Yusuf's saying, and after establishment it is unanimously disliked. Then he said: In my view, the preferred position is that the stratagem for pre-emption is not disliked, but for zakat it is disliked. Question: Is there a stratagem to drop the stratagem? Answer: In Sall al-Anhur, vol. 2, p. 416: There is no stratagem to drop the stratagem, and we have sought it much but did not find it.
Source pages p. 116

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad regarding the ruling on using legal stratagems (hila) to prevent the right of pre-emption (shuf'a) and zakat from becoming established. The key question is whether such a stratagem is permissible or disliked. Imam Muhammad holds that it is makruh because shuf'a is legislated to remove harm, and allowing a stratagem that prevents the harm from being removed defeats the purpose. Imam Abu Yusuf argues that since the right has not yet been established, preventing its coming into existence is not an act of harm or injustice; rather, it is a permissible avoidance. The same difference applies to zakat. Later scholars (such as in Majma' al-Anhur) specify that before the right of shuf'a is established, the fatwa is on Abu Yusuf's view (not disliked), but after the right is established, it is unanimously disliked. The author of Ashraf al-Hidaya expresses his preferred position that for shuf'a, the stratagem is not disliked, but for zakat it is. The passage concludes with a question about whether there is a stratagem to drop the stratagem itself, and the answer is that no such stratagem exists.

Key Terms
حيلة (hīla): A legal stratagem or device to achieve a lawful purpose by indirect means.
شفعة (shuf'a): The right of pre-emption; the right of a co-owner to purchase the share of a new owner when property is sold.
اسقاط (isqāṭ): Dropping or canceling a right before or after it is established.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling on using a legal stratagem to drop the right of pre-emption (shuf'a) before the right is established?
A) It is unanimously disliked.
B) It is not disliked according to Abu Yusuf, but disliked according to Muhammad.
C) It is permissible only if done after the sale is complete.
D) It is forbidden because it contradicts the purpose of shuf'a.

Key Takeaway
Intra-Hanafi dispute on hila: Abu Yusuf permits it before establishment; Muhammad considers it makruh. The later fatwa adopts Abu Yusuf's view before establishment and considers it disliked after, with further nuance between shuf'a and zakat.
