Shuf'a with Multiple Parties: The Rule of Tafarruq al-Safqah
Ruling on shuf'a with multiple parties

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on shuf'a when there are multiple buyers or multiple sellers and explain the underlying principle of tafarruq al-safqah.

Core Idea
If multiple buyers: pre-emptor may pick one share. If multiple sellers: pre-emptor must take all or none—splitting the contract harms the buyer.

In shuf'a (pre-emption), the right to replace the buyer is not absolute. The Hanafi school balances the pre-emptor's right against the buyer's interest in a complete, undivided transaction. This lesson examines two contrasting scenarios from al-Jami' al-Saghir to understand how the principle of tafarruq al-safqah (splitting the contract) governs the pre-emptor's options.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
Note that the passage presents two cases: (A) five buyers from one seller, and (B) one buyer from five sellers. The ruling for each differs based on who would suffer harm from partial pre-emption.
The key is to see which party's contract would be split.
2
State the ruling for each case
For case A, the pre-emptor may take the share of any one buyer. For case B, the pre-emptor must take all shares or leave all. Cannot take only part.
Memorize: multiple buyers → optional; multiple sellers → all-or-nothing.
3
Understand the illah (legal cause)
The difference is tafarruq al-safqah—splitting the contract. In case B, taking part would force the buyer to seek substitute property, causing extra harm. In case A, the contract was already split among buyers; the pre-emptor merely replaces one.
Harm (darar) is the underlying justification.
4
Apply the possession nuance
The same ruling applies whether possession has been taken or not. However, before possession, if some buyers have paid and others not, the pre-emptor cannot take the share of a paying buyer alone because that would split the seller's hand (inconvenience to seller).
After possession, this additional restriction is removed.
5
Test with analogous scenarios
Create hypotheticals: e.g., three buyers from two sellers? Actually the text covers only two patterns. But the principle extends: any case where partial pre-emption would split a single contract (and cause harm) is prohibited.
The criterion is the unity of the contract (ṣafqa).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال واذا اشترى خمسة نفر دارا من رجل فللشفيع ان يأخذ نصيب احدهم وان اشتراها رجل من خمسة اخذها كلها او تركها والفرق ان فى الوجه الثانى باخذ البعض تتفرق الصفقة على المشترى فيتضرر به زيادة الضرر وفى الوجه الأول يقوم الشفيع مقام احدهم فلا تتفرق صفقة
ترجمہ امام محمد نے جامع صغیر میں فرمایا اور جب پانچ آدمیوں نے کسی شخص کا ایک گھر خریدا تو شفیع کو حق ہے کہ ان میں سے کسی ایک کے حصہ کو لے لے اور اگر گھر کو پانچ آدمیوں سے کسی ایک شخص نے خریدا تو شفیع یا تو سارے کولے یا سارے کو چھوڑے اور فرق یہ ہے کہ دوسری صورت میں بعض کو لینے کی وجہ سے مشتری پر صفقہ متفرق ہو جائے گا جس سے وہ زیادہ ضر ر ا ٹھائے گا اور پہلی صورت میں شفیع ان میں سے ایک کے قائم مقام ہوگا تو صدقہ متفرق نہ ہوگا۔ تشریح ہدا یہ جلد ثالث میں بارہا آپ نے تفرق صفقہ کی صورتیں پڑھی ہیں جس کو ممنوع قرار دیا گیا ہے اگر ایک شخص نے پانچ آدمیوں سے ایک گھر خریدا اور شفیع چاہتا ہے کہ میں بکر والے حصہ کو شفعہ میں لے لوں اور باقی حصوں کو چھوڑ دوں تو اس میں مشتری کا ضرر ہے۔ کیونکہ اس کو اتنی جگہ کی ضروری تھی جو اس نے خریدی اگر اس میں سے ایک حصہ شفیع کومل جائے تو مشتری کو اسی کے بقدر کہیں اور جگہ تلاش کر کے خریدنی پڑے گی تا کہ اس کی ضرورت دور ہو تو مشتری کے اوپر تفرق صفقہ لازم آتا ہے جو ممنوع ہے۔ لہذا شفیع کو کہا جائے گا که با تو سارا لو ورنہ سارا چھوڑ دو۔ اور اگر بائع دار ایک شخص ہے اور خریدنے والے مثلاً پانچ افراد ہیں تو شفیع کو بھی یہ حق ہے کہ پورا مکان شفعہ میں لے لے اور یہ بھی حق ہے کہ ان پانچوں میں سے کسی ایک کا لے کر اس کا قائم مقام ہو جائے کیونکہ یہاں تفرق صفقہ لازم نہیں آتا بلکہ بات جوں کی توں ہے اور مشترین پہلے سے متفرق ہیں اور ان میں سے ایک کے قائم مقام شفیع ہوا ہے۔
مشتری قبضہ کر چکا ہو یا نہ کر چکا ہو دونوں صورتوں کا ایک ہی حکم ہے
ولا فرق فى هذا بين ما اذا كان قبل القبض او بعده هو الصحيح الا ان قبل القبض لا يمكنه اخذ نصيب احدهم اذا نقد ما عليه ما لم ينقد الآخر حصته كيلا يؤدى الى تفريق اليد على البائع بمنزلة احد المشتريين بخلاف ما بعد القبض لانه سقطت يد البائع وسواء سمى لكل بعض ثمنا او كان الثمن جملة لان العبرة في هذا التفرق الصفقة لا للثمن وههنا تفريعات ذكرناها في كفاية المنتهى
He said: And if five persons buy a house from one man, then the pre-emptor may take the share of any one of them. And if one man buys a house from five persons, he takes all of it or leaves it. The difference is that in the second case, by taking some, the contract is split on the buyer, causing him additional harm. In the first case, the pre-emptor takes the place of one of them, so the contract is not split. Translation: Imam Muhammad said in al-Jami' al-Saghir: And when five persons bought a house from one person, the pre-emptor has the right to take the share of any one of them. And if one person bought the house from five persons, the pre-emptor either takes all or leaves all. The difference is that in the second case, taking some causes the contract to be split on the buyer (mujtari), resulting in extra harm. In the first case, the pre-emptor stands in the place of one of them, so the contract is not split. Explanation: In this volume of Hidaya, you have often studied the cases of tafarruq al-safqah (splitting of the contract), which is prohibited. If one person buys a house from five persons, and the pre-emptor wants to take only 'Bakr's' share and leave the rest, then there is harm for the buyer because he needed the entire space he bought; if one share goes to the pre-emptor, he will have to find and buy another space of the same size to fulfill his need, so tafarruq al-safqah becomes necessary for him, which is prohibited. Therefore, the pre-emptor is told: either take all or leave all. And if the seller is one person and the buyers are, for example, five individuals, the pre-emptor has the right either to take the entire house or to take the share of one of them and stand in his place, because here tafarruq al-safqah does not occur; rather, the matter remains as it is, and the buyers were already separate, and the pre-emptor stands in the place of one of them. There is no difference whether the buyer has taken possession or not; the ruling is the same. The correct view is that there is no difference before or after possession, except that before possession, he cannot take the share of one of them if he has paid his portion while the others have not paid, to avoid splitting the seller's hand. This is like one of the buyers. After possession, the seller's hand is removed. It is the same whether a price was named for each part or the price was lump sum, because the consideration in this is the splitting of the contract, not the price. And there are further ramifications mentioned in Kifayat al-Muntaha.
Source pages p. 117

Commentary
This passage from al-Jami' al-Saghir presents a ruling on shuf'a involving multiple parties. Two scenarios are contrasted: (1) Multiple buyers from a single seller: the pre-emptor may take the share of any one buyer, because the contract is already between the seller and multiple buyers; taking the place of one buyer does not split a single contract. (2) A single buyer from multiple sellers: the pre-emptor must take all the shares or none, because taking only part would split the single contract the buyer made, causing him harm (tafarruq al-safqah). The commentary explains that this harm arises because the buyer needed the entire property; if part is taken, he must seek alternative space, suffering inconvenience. The same ruling applies whether possession has been taken or not, with a nuance: before possession, if some buyers have paid and others not, the pre-emptor cannot take the share of a paying buyer alone because that would split the seller's hand (i.e., cause the seller to deal with multiple claimants). After possession, this concern vanishes. The ruling is independent of whether the price was specified per share or as a lump sum because the criterion is the splitting of the contract itself.

Key Terms
صفقة (ṣafqa): A sale contract or a single transaction encompassing multiple items.
تفرق الصفقة (tafarruq al-ṣafqa): The splitting of a single sale contract into separate parts, which is considered harmful and thus prohibited.
شفعة (shuf'a): Pre-emption: the right of a co-owner or neighbor to replace the buyer of a property by paying the same price.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If one person buys a house from five different sellers, what is the rule regarding the pre-emptor's right?
A) The pre-emptor can take the share of any one seller.
B) The pre-emptor must take all the shares or leave all.
C) The pre-emptor cannot exercise shuf'a at all.
D) The pre-emptor can take the share of the seller with whom he has a relationship.

Key Takeaway
The pre-emptor's right is conditional: when one buyer from multiple sellers, must take all or none; when multiple buyers from one seller, may take a partial share—the key is whether partial taking would split a single contract and cause harm.

Pre-emption: Multiple Buyers vs Multiple Sellers
Distinction between multiple buyers and multiple sellers in pre-emption

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the two scenarios of shuf'ah (multiple buyers vs multiple sellers) and apply the rule that the pre-emptor must avoid tafarruq al-safqah causing harm to the buyer.

Core Idea
Pre-emptor must take all or leave all when buying from multiple sellers to avoid splitting the transaction.

In this lesson, we examine the Hanafi ruling on pre-emption when the property is sold by multiple sellers to one buyer, or by one seller to multiple buyers. The key principle is the prohibition of tafarruq al-safqah – splitting the transaction in a way that harms the buyer. Understanding this distinction is crucial for correctly applying shuf'ah rights.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
First, recognize the two cases: (1) multiple buyers purchase from one seller; (2) one buyer purchases from multiple sellers. The number of parties affects the ruling.
2
State the ruling for each scenario
In case (1), the pre-emptor may take the share of any one buyer. In case (2), the pre-emptor must take all shares or leave all.
This is the foundational ruling from Imam Muhammad in al-Jami' al-Saghir.
3
Locate the effective cause (illa)
The illa is the harm (darar) caused by splitting the transaction (tafarruq al-safqah). In case (2), taking only a part forces the buyer to seek another property for the remaining need, causing increased harm.
The prohibition of causing harm is a general Shari'ah principle.
4
Compare and contrast the two cases
In case (1), the pre-emptor simply replaces one buyer; the original transaction remains intact. In case (2), the buyer purchased a single unitary property; partial taking splits the contract.
5
Note the nuance before possession
Before possession, the pre-emptor cannot take possession of his share until all other buyers pay their shares, to protect the seller from split possession. After possession, he can take immediately.
This nuance does not change the core ruling but adds a procedural condition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال واذا اشترى خمسة نفر دارا من رجل فللشفيع ان يأخذ نصيب احدهم وان اشتراها رجل من خمسة اخذها كلها او تركها والفرق ان فى الوجه الثانى باخذ البعض تتفرق الصفقة على المشترى فيتضرر به زيادة الضرر وفى الوجه الأول يقوم الشفيع مقام احدهم فلا تتفرق صفقة
ترجمہ امام محمد نے جامع صغیر میں فرمایا اور جب پانچ آدمیوں نے کسی شخص کا ایک گھر خریدا تو شفیع کو حق ہے کہ ان میں سے کسی ایک کے حصہ کو لے لے اور اگر گھر کو پانچ آدمیوں سے کسی ایک شخص نے خریدا تو شفیع یا تو سارے کولے یا سارے کو چھوڑے اور فرق یہ ہے کہ دوسری صورت میں بعض کو لینے کی وجہ سے مشتری پر صفقہ متفرق ہو جائے گا جس سے وہ زیادہ ضرر اٹھائے گا اور پہلی صورت میں شفیع ان میں سے ایک کے قائم مقام ہوگا تو صدقہ متفرق نہ ہوگا۔ تشریح ہدایہ جلد ثالث میں بارہا آپ نے تفرق صفقہ کی صورتیں پڑھی ہیں جس کو ممنوع قرار دیا گیا ہے اگر ایک شخص نے پانچ آدمیوں سے ایک گھر خریدا اور شفیع چاہتا ہے کہ میں بکر والے حصہ کو شفعہ میں لے لوں اور باقی حصوں کو چھوڑ دوں تو اس میں مشتری کا ضرر ہے۔ کیونکہ اس کو اتنی جگہ کی ضروری تھی جو اس نے خریدی اگر اس میں سے ایک حصہ شفیع کومل جائے تو مشتری کو اسی کے بقدر کہیں اور جگہ تلاش کر کے خریدنی پڑے گی تا کہ اس کی ضرورت دور ہو تو مشتری کے اوپر تفرق صفقہ لازم آتا ہے جو ممنوع ہے۔ لہذا شفیع کو کہا جائے گا که با تو سارا لو ورنہ سارا چھوڑ دو۔ اور اگر بائع دار ایک شخص ہے اور خریدنے والے مثلاً پانچ افراد ہیں تو شفیع کو بھی یہ حق ہے کہ پورا مکان شفعہ میں لے لے اور یہ بھی حق ہے کہ ان پانچوں میں سے کسی ایک کا لے کر اس کا قائم مقام ہو جائے کیونکہ یہاں تفرق صفقہ لازم نہیں آتا بلکہ بات جوں کی توں ہے اور مشترین پہلے سے متفرق ہیں اور ان میں سے ایک کے قائم مقام شفیع ہوا ہے۔
مشتری قبضہ کر چکا ہو یا نہ کر چکا ہو دونوں صورتوں کا ایک ہی حکم ہے
ولا فرق فى هذا بين ما اذا كان قبل القبض او بعده هو الصحيح الا ان قبل القبض لا يمكنه اخذ نصيب احدهم اذا نقد ما عليه ما لم ينقد الآخر حصته كيلا يؤدى الى تفريق اليد على البائع بمنزلة احد المشتريين بخلاف ما بعد القبض لانه سقطت يد البائع وسواء سمى لكل بعض ثمنا او كان الثمن جملة لان العبرة في هذا التفرق الصفقة لا للثمن وههنا تفريعات ذكرناها في كفاية المنتهى
ترجمہ اور کوئی فرق نہیں ہے اس میں اسکے درمیان جبکہ قبضہ سے پہلے ہو یا اس کے بعد یہی صحیح ہے مگر قبضہ سے پہلے ان کو ان میں سے ایک کے حصہ کو لینا ممکن نہیں جبکہ وہ مشن ادا کر دے جو اس کے ذمہ ہے جب تک کہ دوسرا اپنے حصہ کو ادا نہ کر دے۔ تا کہ یہ بائع کے اوپر قبضہ کی تفریق کی جانب موصل نہ ہود و مشتریوں میں سے ایک کے درجہ میں بخلاف قبضہ کے بعد کے۔ اس لئے کہ بائع کا قبضہ ساقط ہو چکا ہے اور خواہ بائع ہر حصہ کیلئے شمن متعین کر دے۔ یا شمن مجموعی ہو اس لئے کہ اس میں تفرق صفقہ کا اعتبار ہے نہ کہ تفرق شمن کا اور یہاں کچھ تفریعات ہیں جن کو ہم نے کفایتہ انتہی میں ذکر کیا ہے۔ تشریح مصنف فرماتے ہیں کہ جو مسئلہ بیان کیا گیا ہے اس کا یہی حکم ہے۔ خواہ مشتری قبضہ کر چکا ہو یا قبضہ نہ کیا ہو۔ دونوں صورتوں میں کوئی فرق نہیں ہے۔ البتہ اتنا فرق ضرور ہے کہ اگر مشتری متعدد ہوں اور ابھی تک مشتریوں کا مبیع پر قبضہ نہیں ہوا تھا کہ شفیع نے ان میں سے ایک کا حصہ شفعہ میں لے لیا اور بائع کو اس حصہ کا شمن ادا کر دیا۔ تو جب تک دوسرے شر کا شمن ادا نہیں کریں گے تب تک بائع کو حق ہے کہ وہ شفیع کو اس کا حصہ اسکے حوالہ نہ کرے تا کہ قبضہ کی تفریق کے بارے بائع کی حفاظت ہو سکے۔ جیسا کہ اگر دومشتری ہوں وہاں بھی یہی حکم ہے۔ اور اگر مشتری کا قبضہ ہو چکا ہے تو پھر شفیع ثمن ادا کر کے اپنے حصہ کو قبضہ میں لاسکتا ہے۔ بائع نے ہر حصہ کا شمن علیحدہ بیان کیا ہو یا پور نے گھر کا شمن اکٹھا بیان کیا ہو دونوں صورتوں میں یہی حکم ہے۔
سوال .... اگر شمن مجموعی ہو تو اس کا تفرقہ لازم آئے گا اور آپ نے فرمایا کہ دونوں میں کوئی فرق نہیں ہے؟ جواب ... اتحاد صفقہ کا یہاں اعتبار ہے اتحاد من کا نہیں تو تفرق صفقہ مضر ہے نہ کہ تفرق شمن۔ صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ ہم نے کفایتہ انتہی میں اس مقام پر بہت تفریحات بیان کی ہیں۔
He said: And when five persons buy a house from a man, the pre-emptor may take the share of any one of them. And if one man buys a house from five, he takes all of it or leaves it. The difference is that in the second case, taking some splits the transaction upon the buyer, causing him increased harm. In the first case, the pre-emptor stands in the place of one of them, so the transaction does not split. Translation: Imam Muhammad said in al-Jami' al-Saghir: And when five persons buy a house from a person, the pre-emptor has the right to take the share of any one of them. And if a house is bought by one person from five, the pre-emptor either takes all or leaves all. The difference is that in the second case, taking some causes the transaction to split on the buyer, resulting in greater harm. In the first case, the pre-emptor takes the place of one of them, so the transaction does not split. Commentary: ... There is no difference in this between before possession and after; this is the correct view. But before possession, he cannot take the share of one of them if he pays his share unless the other pays his share, so as not to lead to splitting the hand over the seller, like one of the buyers. Contrary to after possession, because the seller's hand has ceased. And whether the price is specified for each part or the price is lump sum, because the consideration in this is the splitting of the transaction, not the splitting of the price. And here are some ramified issues which we mentioned in Kifayat al-Muntaha. Translation: And there is no difference in this between before possession and after; this is the correct view. But before possession, it is not possible for him to take the share of one of them when he pays what is due from him unless the other pays his share, so that this does not lead to splitting of possession over the seller, like one of the buyers. Contrary to after possession, because the seller's possession has fallen. And whether the seller specifies a price for each part or the price is lump sum, because the consideration in this is the splitting of the transaction, not the splitting of the price. And there are some ramified issues which we mentioned in Kifayat al-Muntaha. Commentary: The author says that the ruling mentioned is the same whether the buyer has taken possession or not. There is no difference between the two cases. However, there is this difference: if there are multiple buyers and they have not yet taken possession of the sold item, and the pre-emptor takes the share of one of them and pays the price to the seller, then until the other buyers pay their shares, the seller has the right not to hand over the share to the pre-emptor, so that the seller is protected from splitting of possession. Just as if there were two buyers, the same ruling applies. And if possession has occurred, then the pre-emptor can pay the price and take possession of his share. Whether the seller specified the price for each share separately or the total price for the whole house, the ruling is the same in both cases. Question: If the price is lump sum, would splitting not be necessary? And you said there is no difference between the two cases? Answer: In this, the unity of the transaction is considered, not the unity of the price. So splitting the transaction is harmful, not splitting the price. The author of Hidayah says: We have mentioned many ramified issues in Kifayat al-Muntaha.
Source pages p. 117

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the Hanafi school regarding pre-emption (shuf'ah). It addresses two scenarios: (1) multiple buyers from one seller, and (2) one buyer from multiple sellers. The key principle is that the pre-emptor (shafi') cannot cause tafarruq al-safqah (splitting of the transaction) to the detriment of the buyer. In the first case, since the buyers are already separate parties, taking one share does not split the original sale contract — the pre-emptor simply replaces one buyer. In the second case, the buyer purchased the entire property as a single transaction; taking only part would force the buyer to seek another property for the remaining need, causing harm. Thus, the pre-emptor must take all or none. The same ruling applies whether or not possession has been taken, but with a nuance before possession: the pre-emptor cannot take possession of his share until all other buyers pay their shares, to avoid splitting the seller's right to retain possession until full payment. The price being lump sum or itemized does not affect the ruling, as the prohibition is on splitting the transaction, not the price. The author refers to further details in his work Kifayat al-Muntaha.

Key Terms
شفعة (shuf'ah): The right of pre-emption whereby a co-owner or neighbour can purchase the sold share from the buyer by paying the price.
تفرق الصفقة (tafarruq al-safqah): The splitting of a single transaction into parts, which is prohibited if it causes harm to the buyer.
صفقة (safqah): A transaction or sale contract; here refers to the unitary act of sale.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If one person buys a house from five co-owners, and the pre-emptor wants to take only the share of one seller, what does Hanafi law require?
A) He may take that share and leave the rest.
B) He must take all shares or leave all.
C) He can take any number of shares.
D) He has no right because the sellers are many.

Key Takeaway
The prohibition of causing harm (darar) by splitting a unitary transaction (tafarruq al-safqah) determines the pre-emptor's obligation to take all or leave all when buying from multiple sellers.

Pre-emption After Partition: The Ruling on an Undivided Half
Ruling with proof on pre-emption after partition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a pre-emptor's right arises after partition and explain why partition binds the pre-emptor.

Core Idea
Partition completes possession, so the pre-emptor cannot undo it.

This passage from al-Hidayah addresses a practical scenario: someone buys an undivided half of a house, the seller later partitions the property with the buyer, and then a pre-emptor appears. The key question is whether the pre-emptor can take the original undivided half or demand a re-partition. The Hanafi answer is clear: the pre-emptor must take the specific half that resulted from the partition, or leave it, because partition (qasama) is considered the completion of possession (tamām al-qabḍ). Understanding this ruling requires grasping the legal effect of partition in Hanafi law.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
The act: a person buys an undivided half of a house. Then the seller (the original owner) makes a partition (qasama) with the buyer, giving each a specific half. Later, a pre-emptor (shafi') claims the right of shuf'a. The ruling: the pre-emptor can only take the half that became the buyer's property after partition, or he can leave it entirely. He cannot take the original undivided half or demand a different share.
2
Understand the reasoning: partition completes possession
The reason given in the text: partition (qisama) is considered 'from the completion of possession' (min tamām al-qabḍ) because it enables full beneficial use (takmīl al-intifā'). In Hanafi law, possession of an undivided share is incomplete until the property is physically divided. Thus, after partition, possession is perfected and cannot be overturned by a third party.
This is supported by the analogy to gifts (hiba): possession in a gift is also completed only after partition.
3
Apply the analogy to gifts
The text invokes the rule that 'possession is completed by partition in gifts' (wa-li-hādhā yatimm al-qabḍ bi-l-qisma fi l-hiba). Just as a donee cannot have full possession of a gift of an undivided share until the property is partitioned, the pre-emptor cannot claim a right that would undo the completed possession of the buyer after partition.
This shows the internal consistency of Hanafi fiqh: the same principle applies across different transactions.
4
Recognise the consequence: pre-emptor cannot overturn possession
The text concludes: 'The pre-emptor does not overturn possession, even if he has benefit in it due to the return of liability (al-uhda) on the seller. Likewise, he does not overturn what is its completion.' In other words, even if the pre-emptor would benefit by reversing the transaction (e.g., by making the seller liable for warranty issues), he cannot break the buyer's completed possession. The partition is treated as a final step that crystallises the buyer's right.
This preserves the stability of property transactions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

ترجمہ امام محمد نے جامع صغیر میں فرمایا اور جس نے خریدا غیر تقسیم شدہ گھر کا نصف پھر اس سے بائع نے بٹوارا کیا تو شفیع اسی نصف کو لے سکتا ہے جو مشتری کے لئے ہوا ہے یا چھوڑ دے اسلئے کہ تحت قبضہ کی تمامیت ہے اسلئے کہ بٹوارہ میں انتفاع کی تکمیل ہے اور اسی وجہ سے بہہ کے اندر بٹوارہ کی وجہ سے قبضہ نام ہوتا ہے اور شفیع قبضہ کونہیں توڑ سکتا ہے۔ اگر چہ اس میں شفیع کا فائدہ ہے عہد ہ بیج کے لوٹ جائے کیوجہ سے بائع کے اوپر تو ایسے ہی اس چیز کوتوڑ سکے گا جو قبضہ کی تمامیت ہے۔ تشریح زید کا ایک گھر ہے اس نے اس کا آدھا حصہ بکر کو فروخت کر دیا اور جو نصف فروخت کیا ہے وہ غیر مقسوم ہے پھر مشتری ( بکر)
He said: And whoever buys an undivided half of a house, and then the seller partitions it with him, the pre-emptor takes the half that became the buyer's or leaves it, because partition completes possession due to its completion of benefit. For this reason, possession is completed by partition in gifts. And the pre-emptor does not overturn possession, even if he has benefit in it due to the return of liability (al-uhda) on the seller. Likewise, he does not overturn what is its completion. Translation: Imam Muhammad said in al-Jami' al-Saghir: And whoever buys an undivided half of a house, then the seller makes a partition with him, then the pre-emptor takes the half that became the buyer's or leaves it, because partition is the completion of possession due to the completion of benefit in it. For this reason, possession is completed by partition in gifts. And the pre-emptor does not overturn possession, even if there is benefit for him in the return of liability to the seller. So similarly, he does not overturn what is its completion. Commentary: Zaid has a house. He sells half of it to Bakr, and the half sold is undivided. Then the buyer (Bakr)...
Source pages p. 118

Commentary
This passage presents a Hanafi ruling on pre-emption when the purchased property is an undivided share and later the seller partitions it. The ruling is from Imam Muhammad's al-Jami' al-Saghir (Zahir al-Riwayah). The key point: partition (qasama) is considered a completion of possession (tamām al-qabḍ) because it enables full beneficial use. Just as in a gift, possession is completed only after partition, here too the pre-emptor cannot undo the partition because he cannot undo possession itself. Therefore, the pre-emptor's right attaches to the specific half that became the buyer's property after partition. He may either take that half (by paying its price) or leave it entirely; he cannot demand the original undivided half or a different portion. The reasoning: once possession is complete through partition, the pre-emptor cannot break it, even if there is a potential benefit for him (like the return of warranty liability to the seller). This ensures stability of transactions and prevents loss to the buyer who has already partly benefited from the partition.

Key Terms
قسمة (qasama / qismah): Partition of jointly owned property into distinct shares, here between seller and buyer of an undivided half.
تمام القبض (tamām al-qabḍ): The completion of possession, achieved through partition because it enables full enjoyment of the property.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a pre-emptor's right arises after the seller has partitioned an undivided half with the buyer, what is the pre-emptor's option according to the passage?
A) He can take the entire house.
B) He can take only the half that became the buyer's share or leave it.
C) He can force a new partition.
D) He loses his right because of the partition.

Key Takeaway
Partition completes possession; thus, a pre-emptor can only take the specific share resulting from the partition, not the original undivided half.

Pre-emption with Multiple Buyers and Lump Sum Price
Explains ruling on pre-emption with multiple buyers and lump sum price

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi ruling on pre-emption when multiple buyers purchase in a single transaction, and explain the seller's right to withhold delivery until all buyers pay their shares.

Core Idea
Unity of transaction (safqa) governs pre-emption, not unity of price; seller may protect against division of possession.

This lesson unpacks a refined ruling from al-Hidayah on shuf'a (right of pre-emption) when two or more persons buy a property together. The key distinction is whether possession has been taken. You will learn the protective measure granted to the seller to avoid being forced to deliver possession in parts, and why a lump-sum price does not alter the ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
We have multiple buyers who purchased a property in one sale (unity of safqa). The pre-emptor seeks to take only one buyer's share.
This is a common but nuanced situation.
2
State the general ruling
The pre-emptor's right is valid whether possession has occurred or not — the ruling is the same in both cases.
No difference in the permissibility of taking the share.
3
Note the seller's protective measure
If possession has not yet been given, the seller may withhold delivery of the taken share until all buyers pay their shares. This prevents division of possession.
Protects seller from being forced to deliver part of the property before full payment.
4
Explain the rationale
The concern is tafriq al-safqa (division of the transaction) not tafriq al-thaman (division of price). Hence, lump sum or separate prices do not affect the ruling.
Unity of the contract is the governing factor.
5
Identify the cross-madhhab dimension
Pre-emption itself is disputed across madhhabs; this detail on multiple buyers may also vary. The Hanafi position is as stated.
Acknowledging valid ikhtilaf.

Source Text

Translation: And there is no difference in it between whether it is before possession or after it; this is correct. But before possession, it is not possible for them to take the share of one of them when he pays the price that is due from him until the other pays his share. So that it does not lead to division of possession over the seller, unlike after possession, because the seller's right to possession has fallen. However, there is this difference: if there are multiple buyers and possession has not yet taken place, and the pre-emptor takes the share of one of them and pays the price to the seller, then until the other [buyer] pays his price, the seller has the right not to hand over that share to the pre-emptor, so that the seller can protect against division of possession. Similarly, if there are two buyers, the same applies. And if the buyer has taken possession, then the pre-emptor can take possession of his share after paying the price. Whether the seller specified the price for each share separately or stated the total price of the house, the ruling is the same. Source pages p. 118

Commentary
This passage clarifies a nuanced rule in pre-emption (shuf'a) when there are multiple buyers. The core ruling is that the pre-emptor's right is the same whether the buyers have taken possession or not. However, a protective measure exists for the seller: if possession has not yet occurred and the pre-emptor takes one buyer's share, the seller may withhold delivery until all buyers pay their shares. This prevents the seller from being forced to deliver possession in parts to different parties. The same applies if the price is stated as a lump sum for the whole property—the focus is on the unity of the transaction (safqa), not the price (thaman). Thus, the pre-emptor must take all or none if the transaction is indivisible. The passage also references al-Hidayah's author's own work Kifayat al-Nihayah for further details.

Key Terms
شفعة (shuf'a): Right of pre-emption: the right of a co-owner or neighbor to purchase a sold share before a stranger.
صفقة (safqa): The sale transaction or contract; unity of safqa means the sale is one indivisible contract.
ثمن (thaman): The price paid for the property; here, whether specified individually or as a lump sum.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi pre-emption, the unity of the transaction (safqa) is paramount; the seller may protect against division of possession by withholding delivery until all buyers pay.

Pre-emptor Cannot Annul Partition with Seller
First scenario: partition between seller and buyer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state that when a buyer partitions with the seller, the pre-emptor cannot annul the partition, and explain the reasoning based on partition completing possession.

Core Idea
Partition with the seller perfects possession; the pre-emptor cannot annul it.

This lesson examines the first scenario from the text: a pre-emptor's right when the buyer and seller partition an undivided share. The key distinction is whether the partition is done by the seller or by another co-owner. Here, partition by the seller completes possession, making it immune from annulment by the pre-emptor.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is partition (qisma) between seller and buyer after sale of an undivided share. The ruling: the pre-emptor cannot annul this partition; he may only take the buyer's share or leave it.
2
Locate the dalil
The text compares to hiba (gift): possession in hiba of an undivided share is not complete until partition. Similarly, in sale, partition completes possession.
The qiyas is based on the common illa of completion of enjoyment.
3
Understand the illa
The effective cause (illa) is 'completion of enjoyment' (takmil al-intifa'). Without partition, the buyer cannot fully enjoy the property individually.
This illa is explicit in the text.
4
Apply the qiyas
Since partition perfects possession in hiba, and the illa of completing enjoyment exists in sale, the same ruling applies: partition perfects possession in sale.
5
Conclude the pre-emptor's limitation
The pre-emptor cannot annul possession (qabd) itself, so he cannot annul what completes it—the partition with the seller.
Any benefit to the pre-emptor, such as transfer of liability, does not change this.

Source Text

کسی کا غیر منقسم مکان خریدنے کے بعد بائع نے اسے تقسیم کر کے ایک حصہ مشتری کیلئے متعین کر دیا تو شفیع کس حصہ کا مستحق ہوگا
قبال ومن اشترى نصف دار غیر مقسوم فقاسمه البائع اخذ الشفيع النصف الذى صار للمشترى او يدع لان القسمة من تمام القبض لما فيها من تكميل الانتفاع ولهذا يتم القبض بالقسمة في الهبة والشفيع لا ينقض القبض وان كان له نفع فيه بعود العهدة على البائع فكذا لا ينقض ما هو من تمامه ترجمہ امام محمد نے جامع صغیر میں فرمایا اور جس نے خریدا غیر تقسیم شدہ گھر کا نصف پھر اس سے بائع نے بٹوارا کیا تو شفیع اسی نصف کو لے سکتا ہے جو مشتری کے لئے ہوا ہے یا چھوڑ دے اسلئے کہ تحت قبضہ کی تمامیت ہے اسلئے کہ بٹوارہ میں انتفاع کی تکمیل ہے اور اسی وجہ سے بہہ [ہبہ؟] کے اندر بٹوارہ کی وجہ سے قبضہ نام ہوتا ہے اور شفیع قبضہ کونہیں تو ڑسکتا ہے۔ اگر چہ اس میں شفیع کا فائدہ ہے عہد ہ بیج [عہدہ بیع؟] کے لوٹ جائے کیوجہ سے بائع کے اوپر تو ایسے ہی اس چیز کوتوڑ سکے گا جو قبضہ کی تمامیت ہے۔ تشریح زید کا ایک گھر ہے اس نے اس کا آدھا حصہ بکر کو فروخت کر دیا اور جو نصف فروخت کیا ہے وہ غیر مقسوم ہے پھر مشتری ( بکر) اور بائع ( زید ) نے بٹوارہ کرلیا تو شفیع کو حق ہے کہ جو حصہ جدھر بھی مشتری کے حصہ میں آیا ہے اس کو شفعہ میں لے لے یا شفعہ چھوڑ دے۔ اگر شفیع یہ چاہے کہ اس ہؤارہ [بٹوارہ؟] کو توڑ دوں اور میں خود بائع سے بڑارہ [بٹوارہ؟] کروں تو شفیع کو حق نہ ہوگا۔ اگر چہ اس میں شفیع کا فائدہ ہے کیونکہ پہلے عبدہ بیچ [عہدہ بیع؟] مشتری کی جانب تھا اور اب وہ بائع کی جانب متحول ہو جائے گا اور اس کا احتمال پیدا ہو جائے گا کہ شفیع کو وہ حصہ مل جائے جو اس کے گھر سے ماما عت [مناسبت؟] ہے۔ مگر کیا کیا جائے شفیع اس بتوارد [بٹوارہ؟] کو تو نہیں سکتا اس لئے کہ ہزارہ [بٹوارہ؟] قبضہ کا ستم [تمام؟] ہے کیونکہ بنوارہ [بٹوارہ؟] کے بغیر منفعت کی تعمیل نہیں ہوسکتی، تو جسے شفیع کو نقض قبضہ کا حق نہیں ایسے ہی نقض قسمت [قسمت؟] کا بھی حق نہ ہوگا۔ اور اگر چاہے صرف وہ حصہ لے سکتا ہے جو مشتری کے بانٹ [بانٹ؟] میں آگیا ہے۔
ہوارہ [بٹوارہ؟] تم قبضہ ہے اس کو مزید واضح کرنے کیلئے فرمایا ولهذا السخ [السک؟] اگر کسی نے ان غیر مقسوم گھر کسی کو ہبہ کر دیا اور موہوب لہ کو قبضہ کرا دیا تو بھی قبضہ نہیں ہوا جب تک کہ : دارہ [بٹوارہ؟] نہ ہو جائے۔ تو جیسے ہبہ کے اندر ہزارہ [بٹوارہ؟] سے قبضہ تام ہوتا ہے ایسے ہی بیچ کے اندر بھی بوار [بٹوارہ؟] تم قبضہ شمار کیا جائے گا دوشریکوں میں سے ایک شریک نے اپنا حصہ تیسرے شخص کے ہاتھ فروخت کر دیا اور جس نے فروخت نہیں کیا اس نے مکان کی تقسیم کر لی تو شفیع اس تقسیم کو ختم کر سکتا ہے یا نہیں
بخلاف ما اذا باع احد الشريكين نصيبه من الدار المشتركة وقاسم المشترى الذى لم يبع حيث يكون للشفيع نقضه لان العقد ما وقع مع الذى قاسم فلم تكن القسمة من تمام القبض الذى هو حكم العقد بل هو رف بـحــكـــم الـــمــلـك فـيــنــقـضــه الشـفيــع كـمـا يــنـقـض بـيـعــــه وهبتــــه
ترجمہ بخلاف اس صورت کے جبکہ دو شریکوں میں سے ایک نے مشترک گھر میں سے اپنا حصہ فروخت کیا ہو اور مشتری نے بٹوارہ کیا اس شخص سے جس نے ( اپنا حصہ ) فروخت نہیں کیا تو شفیع کیلئے اس تقسیم کو توڑنے کا حق ہوگا۔ اس لئے کہ مشتری نے جس کے ساتھ بٹوارہ کیا ہے اس کے ساتھ عقد واقع نہیں ہوا تو یہاں ہؤارہ [بٹوارہ؟] قبضہ کی تمامیت نہیں ہے وہ قبضہ جو کہ عقد کا حکم ہے بلکہ یہ ( مشتری کا ) تصرف ہے ملک کے حکم سے تو اس تصرف کو شفیع تو ڑسکتا ہے جیسا کہ مشتری کی بیع اور ہبہ کو تو ڑ سکتا ہے۔
تشریح پہلی صورت میں مشترکی نے بائع سے بٹوارہ کیا تھا جس کے توڑنے کا شفیع کو حق نہیں دیا گیا۔ اور اگر کسی مکان کے دو مالک ہوں اور ان میں سے ایک نے اپنا حصہ مشترک کو فروخت کر دیا اب اس مشتری نے دوسرے شریک سے جس نے اپنا حصہ نہیں فروخت کیا بوارہ [بٹوارہ؟] کیا تو اس بنوارہ [بٹوارہ؟] کو شفیع تو ڑ سکتا ہے۔
اسلئے کہ پہلی صورت میں قسمت [قسمت؟] تم [تمام؟] قبضہ بے [ہے؟] چونکہ ہوارہ [بٹوارہ؟] بائع سے ہے اور یہاں قسمت [قسمت؟] متم [تمام؟] قبضہ نہیں ہے چونکہ ہوارہ [بٹوارہ؟] بائع سے نہیں بلکہ ایسے شخص سے ہے جو عقد بیع کے اجنبی کے مثل ہے بلکہ یہاں مشتری نے بنوارہ [بٹوارہ؟] کیا ہے ملکیت کے حکم سے یعنی نصف کو خرید کر اس کا مالک ہو گیا۔ اب اس میں اپنی ملکیت کی وجہ سے تصرف کر رہا ہے۔
Regarding one who buys half an undivided house and then the seller partitions with him: The pre-emptor takes the half that became the buyer's or leaves it, because partition completes possession as it completes enjoyment. For this reason, possession is perfected by partition in gift (hiba). And the pre-emptor cannot annul possession, even if there is benefit for him in the return of the liability to the seller. Similarly, he cannot annul what is its completion. Commentary: Imam Muhammad said in al-Jami' al-Saghir: And one who buys half an undivided house, then the seller partitions with him: the pre-emptor takes the half that became the buyer's or leaves it, because partition is completion of possession, since it completes enjoyment, and for this reason possession is perfected by partition in gift. And the pre-emptor cannot annul possession, even if he has benefit in it due to the return of the liability to the seller. So similarly, he cannot annul what is its completion. Explanation: Zayd has a house; he sold half to Bakr, and the sold half is undivided. Then the buyer (Bakr) and seller (Zayd) partitioned. The pre-emptor has the right to take the share that fell to the buyer in pre-emption or to leave it. If the pre-emptor wishes to break this partition and himself partition with the seller, he has no right, even if there is benefit for him because previously the liability of sale was towards the buyer and now it would transfer to the seller, and there would be a possibility that the pre-emptor gets the share adjacent to his house. But what can be done? The pre-emptor cannot break this partition because partition is completion of possession; without partition, enjoyment cannot be completed. Just as the pre-emptor has no right to annul possession, similarly he has no right to annul partition. And if he wishes, he may only take the share that came into the buyer's lot. 

Contrary to the case when one of two partners sold his share from a jointly-owned house, and the buyer partitioned with the one who did not sell: then the pre-emptor has the right to annul it, because the contract was not concluded with the one with whom he partitioned, so the partition is not from the completion of possession which is a ruling of the contract, but rather it is an act by virtue of ownership. So the pre-emptor annuls it just as he annuls his sale and gift. Translation: Contrary to the case when two partners, one sold his share from the jointly-owned house, and the buyer partitioned with the one who did not sell: then the pre-emptor has the right to break this partition, because the contract was not concluded with the one with whom he partitioned. So here the partition is not completion of possession that is the ruling of the contract; rather it is an act by virtue of ownership, so the pre-emptor can break it just as he can break his sale and gift. Explanation: In the first case, the buyer partitioned with the seller, so the pre-emptor was not given the right to break it. And if a house has two owners, and one of them sold his share to a third person, then this buyer partitioned with the other partner (who did not sell), then the pre-emptor can break this partition. Because in the first case, partition was completion of possession since it was with the seller, and here partition is not completion of possession since it is not with the seller but with a person who is like a stranger to the sale contract. Rather here the buyer partitioned by virtue of ownership; i.e., after buying the half, he became its owner, and now he is acting due to his ownership.
Source pages p. 118

Commentary
This passage addresses two scenarios regarding pre-emption (shuf'a) and partition (qisma). The key distinction is whether partition is done by the seller or by the other co-owner. 

First scenario: A person buys half an undivided house from the seller, and then the seller and buyer partition the property. The pre-emptor (shafi') has the option to either take the share that fell to the buyer (through pre-emption) or to abandon his right. However, he cannot annul the partition itself, even if it would be more beneficial for him to have a different division. The reason is that partition perfects possession (qabd) because it completes enjoyment of the property. Just as in a gift (hiba), possession is not considered complete until the property is partitioned if it is shared, similarly in a sale, partition completes possession. Since the pre-emptor cannot annul possession (which is the right of the buyer), he also cannot annul what completes it—the partition. 

Second scenario: Two co-owners of a house; one sells his share to a third party (the buyer). Then the buyer partitions the property with the other co-owner (who did not sell). In this case, the pre-emptor can annul the partition. Why? Because the partition here is not a completion of the possession that arises from the sale contract (since the partition was with the non-selling co-owner, not with the seller). Rather, it is an act of the buyer based on his ownership. Just as the pre-emptor can annul the buyer's sale or gift (i.e., any act that transfers ownership), he can also annul this partition. 

The ruling is from Imam Muhammad in al-Jami' al-Saghir and is explained in al-Hidayah. It illustrates the principle that partition by the seller is part of the delivery of possession, while partition by a third party is a separate disposition subject to pre-emption.

Key Terms
قسمة (qisma): Partition or division of jointly-owned property into separate portions.
شفعة (shuf'a): The right of pre-emption allowing a co-owner or neighbor to purchase a sold share.
قبض (qabd): Possession or taking delivery; in this context, physical control enabling use.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the scenario where a buyer partitions with the seller after purchasing an undivided share, what is the pre-emptor's right regarding that partition?
A) He may annul the partition and demand a new one.
B) He may only take the buyer's share and cannot annul the partition.
C) He may annul the partition only if it is unfair.
D) He has no pre-emption right in this case.

Key Takeaway
Partition with the seller perfects possession; the pre-emptor cannot annul it, even if it would be more beneficial to do so.

Pre-emptor Can Annul Partition with Other Co-Owner
Second scenario: partition between buyer and other co-owner.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the second scenario where the pre-emptor can annul partition—when the buyer partitions with the other co-owner who did not sell—and explain why this partition is not protected as completion of possession.

Core Idea
Partition with a non-seller co-owner is an act of ownership, not completion of possession, so the pre-emptor can annul it.

This lesson addresses the second scenario from the text: a buyer purchases an undivided share from one co-owner and then partitions with the other co-owner (who did not sell). Unlike partition with the seller, this partition is not considered completion of possession from the sale contract; it is an act of ownership that the pre-emptor can annul, just as he can annul the buyer's other dispositions like sale or gift.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and ruling
Two co-owners: One sells his share to a buyer. The buyer then partitions with the other co-owner (who did not sell). The ruling: the pre-emptor can annul this partition.
2
Understand why it is not completion of possession
The partition is not with the seller, so it is not 'from the completion of possession' which is a ruling of the sale contract. The sale contract only involves the seller and the buyer; the other co-owner is a stranger to that contract.
The text says: 'lianna al-aqda ma waqa'a ma'a alladhi qasama' – because the contract was not concluded with the one with whom he partitioned.
3
Classify the partition as an act of ownership
Since the buyer now owns the share, his partition with the other co-owner is a disposition of ownership, similar to selling or gifting the share.
The text equates this partition to the buyer's sale and gift.
4
Apply the pre-emptor's power to annul dispositions
The pre-emptor can annul any transfer of ownership by the buyer, including sale, gift, and now partition, because these affect the pre-emptor's right.
This is consistent with the general rule that shuf'a gives the right to take the sold property from the buyer.
5
Contrast with the first scenario
The key difference: partition with the seller is protected as completion of possession; partition with a third party is not. The pre-emptor can annul the latter, not the former.
This distinction is crucial for applying the correct ruling.

ہوارہ [بٹوارہ؟] تم قبضہ ہے اس کو مزید واضح کرنے کیلئے فرمایا ولهذا السخ [السک؟] اگر کسی نے ان غیر مقسوم گھر کسی کو ہبہ کر دیا اور موہوب لہ کو قبضہ کرا دیا تو بھی قبضہ نہیں ہوا جب تک کہ : دارہ [بٹوارہ؟] نہ ہو جائے۔ تو جیسے ہبہ کے اندر ہزارہ [بٹوارہ؟] سے قبضہ تام ہوتا ہے ایسے ہی بیچ کے اندر بھی بوار [بٹوارہ؟] تم قبضہ شمار کیا جائے گا دوشریکوں میں سے ایک شریک نے اپنا حصہ تیسرے شخص کے ہاتھ فروخت کر دیا اور جس نے فروخت نہیں کیا اس نے مکان کی تقسیم کر لی تو شفیع اس تقسیم کو ختم کر سکتا ہے یا نہیں
بخلاف ما اذا باع احد الشريكين نصيبه من الدار المشتركة وقاسم المشترى الذى لم يبع حيث يكون للشفيع نقضه لان العقد ما وقع مع الذى قاسم فلم تكن القسمة من تمام القبض الذى هو حكم العقد بل هو رف بـحــكـــم الـــمــلـك فـيــنــقـضــه الشـفيــع كـمـا يــنـقـض بـيـعــــه وهبتــــه
ترجمہ بخلاف اس صورت کے جبکہ دو شریکوں میں سے ایک نے مشترک گھر میں سے اپنا حصہ فروخت کیا ہو اور مشتری نے بٹوارہ کیا اس شخص سے جس نے ( اپنا حصہ ) فروخت نہیں کیا تو شفیع کیلئے اس تقسیم کو توڑنے کا حق ہوگا۔ اس لئے کہ مشتری نے جس کے ساتھ بٹوارہ کیا ہے اس کے ساتھ عقد واقع نہیں ہوا تو یہاں ہؤارہ [بٹوارہ؟] قبضہ کی تمامیت نہیں ہے وہ قبضہ جو کہ عقد کا حکم ہے بلکہ یہ ( مشتری کا ) تصرف ہے ملک کے حکم سے تو اس تصرف کو شفیع تو ڑسکتا ہے جیسا کہ مشتری کی بیع اور ہبہ کو تو ڑ سکتا ہے۔
تشریح پہلی صورت میں مشترکی نے بائع سے بٹوارہ کیا تھا جس کے توڑنے کا شفیع کو حق نہیں دیا گیا۔ اور اگر کسی مکان کے دو مالک ہوں اور ان میں سے ایک نے اپنا حصہ مشترک کو فروخت کر دیا اب اس مشتری نے دوسرے شریک سے جس نے اپنا حصہ نہیں فروخت کیا بوارہ [بٹوارہ؟] کیا تو اس بنوارہ [بٹوارہ؟] کو شفیع تو ڑ سکتا ہے۔
اسلئے کہ پہلی صورت میں قسمت [قسمت؟] تم [تمام؟] قبضہ بے [ہے؟] چونکہ ہوارہ [بٹوارہ؟] بائع سے ہے اور یہاں قسمت [قسمت؟] متم [تمام؟] قبضہ نہیں ہے چونکہ ہوارہ [بٹوارہ؟] بائع سے نہیں بلکہ ایسے شخص سے ہے جو عقد بیع کے اجنبی کے مثل ہے بلکہ یہاں مشتری نے بنوارہ [بٹوارہ؟] کیا ہے ملکیت کے حکم سے یعنی نصف کو خرید کر اس کا مالک ہو گیا۔ اب اس میں اپنی ملکیت کی وجہ سے تصرف کر رہا ہے۔
Regarding one who buys half an undivided house and then the seller partitions with him: The pre-emptor takes the half that became the buyer's or leaves it, because partition completes possession as it completes enjoyment. For this reason, possession is perfected by partition in gift (hiba). And the pre-emptor cannot annul possession, even if there is benefit for him in the return of the liability to the seller. Similarly, he cannot annul what is its completion. Commentary: Imam Muhammad said in al-Jami' al-Saghir: And one who buys half an undivided house, then the seller partitions with him: the pre-emptor takes the half that became the buyer's or leaves it, because partition is completion of possession, since it completes enjoyment, and for this reason possession is perfected by partition in gift. And the pre-emptor cannot annul possession, even if he has benefit in it due to the return of the liability to the seller. So similarly, he cannot annul what is its completion. Explanation: Zayd has a house; he sold half to Bakr, and the sold half is undivided. Then the buyer (Bakr) and seller (Zayd) partitioned. The pre-emptor has the right to take the share that fell to the buyer in pre-emption or to leave it. If the pre-emptor wishes to break this partition and himself partition with the seller, he has no right, even if there is benefit for him because previously the liability of sale was towards the buyer and now it would transfer to the seller, and there would be a possibility that the pre-emptor gets the share adjacent to his house. But what can be done? The pre-emptor cannot break this partition because partition is completion of possession; without partition, enjoyment cannot be completed. Just as the pre-emptor has no right to annul possession, similarly he has no right to annul partition. And if he wishes, he may only take the share that came into the buyer's lot. 

Contrary to the case when one of two partners sold his share from a jointly-owned house, and the buyer partitioned with the one who did not sell: then the pre-emptor has the right to annul it, because the contract was not concluded with the one with whom he partitioned, so the partition is not from the completion of possession which is a ruling of the contract, but rather it is an act by virtue of ownership. So the pre-emptor annuls it just as he annuls his sale and gift. Translation: Contrary to the case when two partners, one sold his share from the jointly-owned house, and the buyer partitioned with the one who did not sell: then the pre-emptor has the right to break this partition, because the contract was not concluded with the one with whom he partitioned. So here the partition is not completion of possession that is the ruling of the contract; rather it is an act by virtue of ownership, so the pre-emptor can break it just as he can break his sale and gift. Explanation: In the first case, the buyer partitioned with the seller, so the pre-emptor was not given the right to break it. And if a house has two owners, and one of them sold his share to a third person, then this buyer partitioned with the other partner (who did not sell), then the pre-emptor can break this partition. Because in the first case, partition was completion of possession since it was with the seller, and here partition is not completion of possession since it is not with the seller but with a person who is like a stranger to the sale contract. Rather here the buyer partitioned by virtue of ownership; i.e., after buying the half, he became its owner, and now he is acting due to his ownership.
Source pages p. 118

Commentary
This passage addresses two scenarios regarding pre-emption (shuf'a) and partition (qisma). The key distinction is whether partition is done by the seller or by the other co-owner. 

First scenario: A person buys half an undivided house from the seller, and then the seller and buyer partition the property. The pre-emptor (shafi') has the option to either take the share that fell to the buyer (through pre-emption) or to abandon his right. However, he cannot annul the partition itself, even if it would be more beneficial for him to have a different division. The reason is that partition perfects possession (qabd) because it completes enjoyment of the property. Just as in a gift (hiba), possession is not considered complete until the property is partitioned if it is shared, similarly in a sale, partition completes possession. Since the pre-emptor cannot annul possession (which is the right of the buyer), he also cannot annul what completes it—the partition. 

Second scenario: Two co-owners of a house; one sells his share to a third party (the buyer). Then the buyer partitions the property with the other co-owner (who did not sell). In this case, the pre-emptor can annul the partition. Why? Because the partition here is not a completion of the possession that arises from the sale contract (since the partition was with the non-selling co-owner, not with the seller). Rather, it is an act of the buyer based on his ownership. Just as the pre-emptor can annul the buyer's sale or gift (i.e., any act that transfers ownership), he can also annul this partition. 

The ruling is from Imam Muhammad in al-Jami' al-Saghir and is explained in al-Hidayah. It illustrates the principle that partition by the seller is part of the delivery of possession, while partition by a third party is a separate disposition subject to pre-emption.

Key Terms
قسمة (qisma): Partition of jointly-owned property into separate portions.
شفعة (shuf'a): The right of pre-emption to purchase a sold share.
قبض (qabd): Possession; in this context, the seller's delivery of the sold item.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the scenario where the buyer partitions with the other co-owner (not the seller), what is the pre-emptor's right?
A) He cannot annul the partition because it is valid.
B) He may annul the partition because it is not completion of possession.
C) He must accept the partition and pay the price.
D) He can only annul if the partition is unfair.

Key Takeaway
A partition between the buyer and a non-selling co-owner is not protected; the pre-emptor can annul it as an act of ownership.

Buyu — Sales and Trade
intermediate
8 min
Master's Preemption When a Ma'dhun Slave Sells a House
Ruling on master's preemption due to slave's sale

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two cases for a master's preemption right when his ma'dhun slave sells a house and explain the underlying analogy (qiyas).

Core Idea
Master's preemption depends on whether the slave's sale benefits creditors or the master.

This lesson examines a specific ruling from Imam Muhammad's al-Jami' al-Saghir regarding the right of preemption (shuf'ah) when a ma'dhun slave sells a house. The ruling hinges on a critical condition: whether the slave has debt covering his property. By understanding the legal analogy (qiyas) that preemption is treated like a purchase, you will be able to derive the correct ruling in each scenario.

Guided Path
1
State the act and its ruling
Identify the act under consideration: a ma'dhun slave selling a house. The ruling is that the master may or may not have the right of preemption (shuf'ah).
2
Identify the condition
Determine the key condition that changes the ruling: whether the slave has a debt that covers his entire property (dayn mustaghriq).
3
Explain the analogy (qiyas)
Understand that preemption is analogous to a purchase because it involves acquiring ownership in exchange for a price (tamalluk bi al-thaman). This analogy means the person for whom the sale is made (the beneficiary) cannot claim preemption.
4
Determine the beneficiary
If the slave has debt, the sale benefits the creditors, not the master. Therefore, the master is a third party and can preempt. If no debt, the sale benefits the master himself, so he cannot preempt.
5
Apply to factual scenarios
Given a specific scenario with a ma'dhun slave, determine whether the slave has debt or not, and then state whether the master has preemption, citing the reasoning.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال ومن باع دارا وله عبد ماذون عليه دين فله الشفعة وكذا اذا كان العبد هو البائع فلمولاه الشفعة لان الأخذ بالشفعة تملك بالثمن فينزل منزلة الشراء وهذا لانه مفيد لانه يتصرف للغرماء بخلاف ما اذا يـــكـــــن عـــليـه دين لانه يبيـ ه لمولاه ولا شفعة لمن بيع له

ترجمہ (امام محمد نے جامع صغیر میں ) فرمایا اور جس نے گھر بیچا اور اس کا غلام مازون ہے۔ جس کے اوپر قرض ہے تو غلام کیلئے شفعہ ہوگا اور ایسے ہی جبکہ غلام بائع ہو تو اس کے مولیٰ کیلئے شفعہ ہو گا اسلئے کہ شفعہ میں شمن کے عوض مالک بننا ہے تو اس کو ( شفعہ میں لینے کو ) شراء کے درجہ میں اتار لیا جائے گا اور یہ اسلئے کہ یہ بیچ مفید ہے اسلئے کہ غلام اپنے قرض خواہوں کیلئے تصرف کرتا ہے۔ بخلاف اس صورت کے جبکہ اس کے اوپر قرض نہ ہو اسلئے کہ غلام اس کو اپنے مولیٰ کیلئے فروخت کرتا ہے اور جس کیلئے فروخت کیا جائے اس کیلئے شفعہ نہیں ہے۔

تشریح . اگر آقا اپنے غلام کو تجارت کی اجازت دیدے تو اس کی خرید و فروخت جائز ہوا کرتی ہے اور اس غلام کو غلام مازون کہا جاتا ہے۔ پھر اس کی تفصیل یہ ہے کہ جو کچھ اس کے قبضہ میں ہے وہ سب اس کے مولی کا ہے۔ اس کی بیع اور اس کی شرط سب مولی کیلئے ہوتی ہے اور یہ جب ہے جبکہ غلام پر اتنا قرضہ نہ ہو جو اس کی گردن کو محیط ہو ۔ ورنہ اگر اس پر اتنا قرضہ ہو جو اس کی گردن کو محیط ہے تو مولیٰ پر یہ ضروری نہ ہوگا کہ وہ اس کا قرض ادا کرے۔ البتہ اگر وہ ادا کرے تو ٹھیک ورنہ اس غلام کو فروخت کر کے غرماء کا قرض ادا کیا جائے اور غلام پر قرض ہونے کی صورت میں اس کی بیع وشراء مولیٰ کیلئے نہیں بلکہ غرماء کیلئے ہوگی ۔ جب یہ تفصیل ذہن نشین ہوگئی تو اب سنئے ۔ ایک غلام مازون نے ایک مکان بغرض تجارت خرید رکھا ہے اب وہ اس کو فروخت کرتا ہے اور اس کے جوار میں آقا کا گھر ہے تو مولی کو شفعہ ملے گا یا نہیں۔ تو اگر غلام مازون مدیون ہے تو شفعہ ملے گا اور اگر مدیون نہ ہو تو شفعہ نہیں ملے گا۔ اس لئے کہ پہلی صورت میں اس کی بیع و شراء مولی کیلئے نہیں ہے تو شفعہ سے کوئی چیز مانع نہیں ہے۔ اور دوسری صورت میں اس کی بیچ و شراء مولی کیلئے ہوتی ہے اسلئے مولیٰ کو شفعہ نہیں ملے گا۔

البتہ شرط کی صورت میں صورت، ثانیہ میں بھی مولیٰ کو شفعہ ملے گا جس کی تفصیل ماقبل میں اصل کلی کے ضمن میں گذر چکی ہے جہاں کہا گیا تھا کہ جس کیلئے بیچا جائے اس کیلئے شفعہ نہیں ہے اور جس کیلئے خریدا جائے اس کیلئے شفعہ ہے۔ لان الاخذ بالشفعة الح - شفعہ میں لینا شراء کے درجہ میں ہے اور جب غلام پر دین مستغرق ہو اس وقت غلام اور مولیٰ میں سے ایک کا دوسرے سے خریدنا جائز ہوتا ہے تو ایسے ہی شفعہ میں لینا بھی جائز ہوگا ۔
He (Imam Muhammad) said: And whoever sells a house while he has a ma'dhun slave who has a debt, then the slave has preemption. Similarly, if the slave is the seller, his master has preemption, because taking by preemption is ownership in lieu of price, so it is treated like purchase. And this is because it is beneficial, as the slave transacts for the creditors. Contrary to when he has no debt, because then the slave sells for his master, and there is no preemption for the one for whom it is sold. Translation: (Imam Muhammad said in al-Jami' al-Saghir) And whoever sold a house and he has a ma'dhun slave upon whom is debt, then the slave has preemption. Similarly, when the slave is the seller, then the master has preemption, because preemption is becoming owner in exchange for price, so it is placed in the position of purchase. And this is because it is beneficial, as the slave transacts for the creditors. Contrary to the case when he does not have debt, because the slave sells it for his master, and there is no preemption for the one for whom it is sold. Explanation: If a master gives his slave permission to trade, then his buying and selling are valid, and that slave is called a ma'dhun slave. Then its detail is that whatever is in his possession belongs to his master. His sale and his condition are all for the master. And this is when the slave does not have so much debt that encompasses his neck. Otherwise, if he has such debt that encompasses his neck, then the master is not required to pay it. If he pays, fine; otherwise, the slave is sold and the creditors' debt is paid. In the case of the slave having debt, his sale and purchase are not for the master but for the creditors. Now that this detail is understood, listen: A ma'dhun slave bought a house for trade, and now he sells it, and next to it is the master's house. Does the master get preemption? If the ma'dhun slave is indebted, then he gets preemption; if he is not indebted, then he does not get preemption. Because in the first case, his sale and purchase are not for the master, so nothing prevents preemption. In the second case, his sale and purchase are for the master, so the master does not get preemption. However, in the case of a condition, in the second case also the master will get preemption, the detail of which has passed earlier in the general principle, where it was said: There is no preemption for the one for whom it is sold, and there is preemption for the one for whom it is purchased. Because taking by preemption is in the position of purchase. And when the slave has debt covering him, it is permissible for one of the slave and the master to buy from the other, so similarly taking by preemption will be permissible.
Source pages p. 120

Commentary
This passage discusses the scenario of a ma'dhun slave (a slave permitted to trade) who sells a house. The ruling depends on whether the slave has a debt that covers his entire property. If the slave has debt, his sale is for the benefit of his creditors, not for his master. Therefore, the master retains the right of preemption as a neighbor. If the slave has no debt, his sale is considered for his master, and the master cannot claim preemption because one cannot claim preemption for a property sold to oneself. The reasoning is that taking by preemption is analogous to a purchase (tamalluk bi al-thaman). The text also notes an exception: if there is a condition, the master might still get preemption, but this is based on a general principle that the one for whom property is purchased is entitled to preemption.

Key Terms
عبد مأذون (abd ma'dhun): A slave permitted by his master to engage in trade.
دين مستغرق (dayn mustaghriq): Debt that covers all property of the slave, making him insolvent.
غرماء (ghurama'): Creditors of the slave.
شفعة (shuf'ah): Preemption; the right to acquire property sold to another, typically due to co-ownership or adjacency.
تملك بالثمن (tamalluk bi al-thaman): Ownership acquired by paying a price; used to equate preemption with purchase.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When does a master have the right of preemption if his ma'dhun slave sells a house?
A) Always, because the slave's property belongs to the master
B) Only if the slave has no debt
C) Only if the slave has debt
D) Only if the master is present

Key Takeaway
A master's preemption right over his ma'dhun slave's sale of a house depends on whether the slave has debt; if yes, preemption is allowed; if no, it is not.

Buyu — Sales and Trade
intermediate
8 min
Shuf'ah Rights When a Ma'dhun Slave Sells Property
Ruling with proof on shuf'ah for master of a ma'dhun slave, distinguishing based on debt

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that a master's right of shuf'ah depends on whether his ma'dhun slave is indebted, and explain the qiyas that treats shuf'ah as equivalent to purchase.

Core Idea
A master's shuf'ah arises only when the slave's sale is not for the master — debt severs the nexus.

This lesson examines a nuanced rule from the Hanafi school: when a ma'dhun slave (a slave permitted to trade) sells property, does his master have the right of preemption (shuf'ah)? The answer depends critically on whether the slave is burdened with debt. The ruling is derived by analogizing shuf'ah to a purchase, using the principle that shuf'ah transfers ownership for compensation just like a sale.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal act and parties
The central act is the master's claim of shuf'ah when his ma'dhun slave sells a house. Identify the agent (slave), the principal (master), and the property (adjacent to master's house).
2
Recognize the two scenarios: slave indebted vs. not indebted
The passage distinguishes two cases: (1) the slave has debt that encompasses his value (dayn mustaghriq); (2) the slave has no such debt. The ruling on shuf'ah differs in each.
Debt 'encompasses' means the slave cannot be sold without paying it off.
3
Understand the underlying principle (qiyas)
Shuf'ah is treated as equivalent to a purchase because ownership is taken in exchange for the price. The text states: 'taking through shuf'ah is placed in the position of purchase' (al-akhdh bi al-shuf'ah ka al-shira').
This qiyas is the core proof for the ruling.
4
Apply the principle to each scenario
When the slave is indebted, his sale is for the creditors, not the master. Thus the master is an outsider and can claim shuf'ah. When the slave has no debt, the sale is deemed for the master himself, so he cannot claim shuf'ah (it would be like taking from himself).
The principle: shuf'ah accrues to the one for whom the purchase is effectively made.
5
Note the exception concerning a condition (shart)
The text adds that even in the second case (no debt), if there is a specific condition, the master may still have shuf'ah. This refers to a pre-existing arrangement between master and slave, e.g., the master had permitted the slave to trade on condition that certain sales benefit the slave's own account.
The condition effectively severs the master's nexus, restoring the master's shuf'ah.

ترجمہ (امام محمد نے جامع صغیر میں ) فرمایا اور جس نے گھر بیچا اور اس کا غلام مازون ہے۔ جس کے اوپر قرض ہے تو غلام کیلئے شفعہ ہوگا اور ایسے ہی جبکہ غلام بائع ہو تو اس کے مولیٰ کیلئے شفعہ ہو گا اسلئے کہ شفعہ میں شمن کے عوض مالک بننا ہے تو اس کو ( شفعہ میں لینے کو ) شراء کے درجہ میں اتار لیا جائے گا اور یہ اسلئے کہ یہ بیچ مفید ہے اسلئے کہ غلام اپنے قرض خواہوں کیلئے تصرف کرتا ہے۔ بخلاف اس صورت کے جبکہ اس کے اوپر قرض نہ ہو اسلئے کہ غلام اس کو اپنے مولیٰ کیلئے فروخت کرتا ہے اور جس کیلئے فروخت کیا جائے اس کیلئے شفعہ نہیں ہے۔ تشریح . اگر آقا اپنے غلام کو تجارت کی اجازت دیدے تو اس کی خرید و فروخت جائز ہوا کرتی ہے اور اس غلام کو غلام مازون کہا جاتا ہے۔ پھر اس کی تفصیل یہ ہے کہ جو کچھ اس کے قبضہ میں ہے وہ سب اس کے مولی کا ہے۔ اس کی بیع اور اس کی شرط سب مولی کیلئے ہوتی ہے اور یہ جب ہے جبکہ غلام پر اتنا قرضہ نہ ہو جو اس کی گردن کو محیط ہو ۔ ورنہ اگر اس پر اتنا قرضہ ہو جو اس کی گردن کو محیط ہے تو مولیٰ پر یہ ضروری نہ ہوگا کہ وہ اس کا قرض ادا کرے۔ البتہ اگر وہ ادا کرے تو ٹھیک ورنہ اس غلام کو فروخت کر کے غرماء کا قرض ادا کیا جائے اور غلام پر قرض ہونے کی صورت میں اس کی بیع وشراء مولیٰ کیلئے نہیں بلکہ غرماء کیلئے ہوگی ۔ جب یہ تفصیل ذہن نشین ہوگئی تو اب سنئے ۔ ایک غلام مازون نے ایک مکان بغرض تجارت خرید رکھا ہے اب وہ اس کو فروخت کرتا ہے اور اس کے جوار میں آقا کا گھر ہے تو مولی کو شفعہ ملے گا یا نہیں۔ تو اگر غلام مازون مدیون ہے تو شفعہ ملے گا اور اگر مدیون نہ ہو تو شفعہ نہیں ملے گا۔ اس لئے کہ پہلی صورت میں اس کی بیع و شراء مولی کیلئے نہیں ہے تو شفعہ سے کوئی چیز مانع نہیں ہے۔ اور دوسری صورت میں اس کی بیچ و شراء مولی کیلئے ہوتی ہے اسلئے مولیٰ کو شفعہ نہیں ملے گا۔

البتہ شرط کی صورت میں صورت، ثانیہ میں بھی مولیٰ کو شفعہ ملے گا جس کی تفصیل ماقبل میں اصل کلی کے ضمن میں گذر چکی ہے جہاں کہا گیا تھا کہ جس کیلئے بیچا جائے اس کیلئے شفعہ نہیں ہے اور جس کیلئے خریدا جائے اس کیلئے شفعہ ہے۔ لان الاخذ بالشفعة الح - شفعہ میں لینا شراء کے درجہ میں ہے اور جب غلام پر دین مستغرق ہو اس وقت غلام اور مولیٰ میں سے ایک کا دوسرے سے خریدنا جائز ہوتا ہے تو ایسے ہی شفعہ میں لینا بھی جائز ہوگا۔
Translation: (Imam Muhammad said in Jami' al-Saghir) And whoever sold a house while his slave is ma'dhun (permitted to trade) and has debt upon him, then the slave has shuf'ah. Similarly, when the slave is the seller, his master has shuf'ah, because in shuf'ah, ownership is taken in exchange for the price, so taking through shuf'ah is placed in the position of purchase. And this is because this sale is beneficial, as the slave transacts for his creditors. Unlike the case when he has no debt, because the slave sells it for his master, and the one for whom it is sold has no shuf'ah. Explanation: If the master permits his slave to trade, his buying and selling are valid, and this slave is called ghulam ma'dhun. The details: whatever is in his possession belongs to his master. His sale and purchase are for the master, and this is when the slave does not have debt encompassing him. Otherwise, if he has debt encompassing him, the master is not obliged to pay his debt; but if he pays, it's fine, otherwise the slave is sold to pay the creditors. In the case of debt, his sale and purchase are not for the master but for the creditors. Now, a ma'dhun slave bought a house for trade, then sells it, and adjacent to it is the master's house. Does the master get shuf'ah? If the ma'dhun slave is indebted, shuf'ah is given; if not indebted, shuf'ah is not given. Because in the first case, his sale and purchase are not for the master, so nothing prevents shuf'ah. In the second case, his sale and purchase are for the master, so the master does not get shuf'ah. However, in the case of a condition (shart), the master gets shuf'ah in the second case as well, as detailed earlier in the general principle that the one for whom it is sold has no shuf'ah, and the one for whom it is bought has shuf'ah. Because taking through shuf'ah is in the position of purchase, and when the slave has encompassing debt, it is permissible for one of them (slave and master) to buy from the other, so similarly, taking through shuf'ah is permissible.
Source pages p. 121

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the Hanafi school regarding the right of shuf'ah (preemption) when a ma'dhun slave (a slave permitted to trade) sells property. The author begins by stating the ruling from Imam Muhammad's Jami' al-Saghir: If a ma'dhun slave who has debts sells a house, then the slave himself has shuf'ah (as buyer) and similarly if the slave is the seller, the master has shuf'ah. The reason given is that shuf'ah is like a purchase in that it transfers ownership in exchange for the price, so it is treated as a purchase. The distinction hinges on whether the slave has debt: if he has debt, his sale is for the benefit of his creditors, not for the master; thus the master can claim shuf'ah. If he has no debt, the sale is deemed to be for the master, so the master cannot claim shuf'ah because the sale is effectively his own. The author then provides a detailed explanation (tashreeh) clarifying the concept of a ma'dhun slave and the effect of debt. He explains that a slave permitted to trade owns nothing; his acquisitions belong to the master unless the slave is burdened with debt that encompasses him, in which case his transactions are for the creditors. In the scenario, if a ma'dhun slave buys a house for trade and then sells it, the master's right to shuf'ah depends on whether the slave is indebted. If indebted, the sale is for creditors, so the master can claim shuf'ah. If not indebted, the sale is for the master, so he cannot claim it. The author also mentions an exception involving a condition (shart) in the second case, referring back to a general principle that shuf'ah is for the one for whom the purchase is made. The proof is the analogy (qiyas) that shuf'ah is equivalent to purchase, and just as a slave with encompassing debt may buy from the master, so too may he take by shuf'ah.

Key Terms
غلام مازون (ghulam ma'dhun): A slave whom the master has permitted to engage in trade, whose transactions are valid but may be for the master or creditors depending on debt status.
شفعة (shuf'ah): The right of preemption: a neighbor or co-owner may purchase sold property by paying the price, taking it from the buyer.
دین مستغرق (dayn mustaghriq): Debt that encompasses the slave's value, such that the slave cannot be sold without paying it off; his transactions are then for creditors.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A ma'dhun slave with no debt sells a house adjacent to his master's house. Does the master have shuf'ah?
A) Yes, because the master is the owner of the slave.
B) No, because the sale is considered for the master, so he cannot claim shuf'ah against himself.
C) Yes, because shuf'ah is always given to neighbors.
D) No, because a slave cannot trigger shuf'ah at all.

Key Takeaway
The master's shuf'ah is contingent on the slave's debt: debt shifts the sale's benefit to creditors, making the master an eligible claimant.

Buyu — Sales and Trade
intermediate
8 min
Guardian's Relinquishment of Minor's Shuf'ah: Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on guardian's authority over minor's shuf'ah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two intra-Hanafi positions on a guardian's relinquishment of a minor's shuf'ah, compare their proofs (qiyas), and identify the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
Guardians can give up a minor's shuf'ah because it is like trade, not a fixed right.

This passage presents a classical dispute within the Hanafi school: Can a father or wasi forfeit the right of preemption (shuf'ah) on behalf of a minor child? Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf (the Shaykhayn) say yes; Muhammad and Zufar say no, and the minor reclaims the right upon maturity. The author of Ashraf al-Hidayah rules with the Shaykhayn, providing a clear example of how ijtihad operates within a single madhhab.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position of the Shaykhayn
Identify that Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf permit the father or wasi to relinquish the minor's shuf'ah. This is the relied-upon view (mufta bihi).
2
Identify the opposing view within the Hanafi school
Muhammad and Zufar hold that the minor retains the right until maturity; the guardian cannot void it.
3
Follow the opponent's proof (qiyas to diyah and qisas)
Muhammad and Zufar analogize shuf'ah to fixed rights like diyah (blood-money) and qisas (retaliation) that are firmly established for the minor and cannot be waived by a guardian. Invalidating shuf'ah would harm the minor, contradicting its purpose.
4
Analyse the Shaykhayn's response and alternative analogy
The Shaykhayn respond by analogizing shuf'ah to trade (tijarah). Guardians have discretionary authority (wilaya nazariyya) over the minor's financial deals; they can reject an offer of sale, and similarly they can decide to leave shuf'ah if it is not beneficial. Even silence (not claiming) is evidence of abandonment.
The dispute is conditioned on the sale being at fair value ('inda bai' bi-mithli qimatiha).
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf and tarjih
Practical consequence: Under the Shaykhayn, the minor permanently loses shuf'ah if guardian relinquishes; under Muhammad/Zufar, the minor can reclaim it upon maturity. The author declares the Shaykhayn's view as correct (al-sahih), citing the narration in Kitab al-Wakalah.
